98. Microraptor has a flat dorsal surface on its distal caudals (coding in Turner et al., 2007).

100. Microraptor is polymorphic, with some specimens having over 24 caudals (Hwang et al., 2002; Ji, 2002).

101. Microraptor has anteroposteriorly elongate anterior chevrons (Ji, 2002).

105. Microraptor has longer lateral gastralia than medial gastralia (unpublished photo of IVPP V13352).

106. Microraptor is polymorphic as some specimens have fused sterna (Xu et al., 2003; Czerkas et al., 2002).

112. Microraptor has a deep coracoid (Hwang et al. 2002; Xu et al., 2003).

115. Microraptor is polymorphic, as NGMC 00-12-A has a more highly angled deltopectoral crest (Ji, 2002).

118. Microraptor (coding in Xu and Zhang, 2005) has a transversely flattened distal ulna.

120. The Microraptor holotype preserves the ulnare in medial view (identified as a 'fourth carpal' by Xu et al., 2000, with their supposed ulnare probably being distal carpal III), based on its resemblence to Allosaurus. NGMC 00-12-A (Ji, 2002) does not fully exposed either ulnare, though one is largely oval so may be in distal view. The ulnare in IVPP V13352 also appears to be oval (unpublished photo), so is coded as derived (as in Hwang et al., coding) for lacking a flat edge.

121. Microraptor has fused distal carpals I and II (Xu et al., 2000; Ji, 2002).

123. Microraptor is polymorphic, as CAGS 20-7-004 has a small semilunate carpal (Hwang et al., 2002), while those of the holotype (Xu et al., 2000) and NGMC 00-12-A (Ji, 2002) are large.

127. Microraptor's (CAGS 20-8-001; Hwang et al., 2002) manual ungual I is no larger compared to II than those of Conchoraptor or "Ingenia", which were coded as plesiomorphic. Those of other Microraptor specimens are even smaller. It is recoded 0.

129. Microraptor has only a small ventral hook on its preacetabular process (Hwang et al., 2002).

132. Microraptor lacks a deep brevis fossa (Xu et al., 2000).

136. Microraptor lacks a proximodorsal ischial process (Xu et al., 2000; Hwang et al., 2002).

139. Microraptor lacks obturator process contact with the pubis (coding in Xu and Zhang, 2005).

140. Microraptor has an obturator notch (Xu et al., 2000, 2003; Hwang et al., 2002).

150. Microraptor has a deep groove between its anterior and greater trochanters (Hwang et al., 2002).

159. Microraptor lacks a deep proximomedial fibular fossa (Hwang et al., 2002).

168. Microraptor's metatarsal III is only very slightly ginglymoid (Hwang et al., 2002), so should be coded 0.

169. Microraptor lacks an arctometatarsus (White, 2009).

176. Microraptor lacks a sharply angled postorbital process on its frontal (coding in Xu and Zhang, 2005).

177. Microraptor has a second premaxillary tooth much larger than the third and fourth (Ji, 2002).

181. Microraptor has a triangular dentary (Hwang et al., 2002; Ji, 2002).

182. Microraptor cannot be coded for internal mandibular fenestra size, as the prearticular is poorly preserved in described specimens (Xu et al., 2000).

183. Microraptor lacks a zygapophyseal ridge on its sacrals (Hwang et al., 2002).

184. Microraptor has a naris which overlaps the antorbital fossa (coding in Xu and Zhang, 2005).

201. Microraptor has a rounded internarial bar (coding in Hwang et al., 2004).

205. Microraptor lacks a strongly flattened metatarsal IV (White, 2009).

206. Microraptor has a short pubic apron (Hwang et al., 2002).

208. Microraptor lacks an especially robust metatarsal IV (Hwang et al., 2002; White, 2009).

 

Xu et al., 2002 on Incisivosaurus

5. As redefined above, Incisivosaurus lacks a subotic recess, so must be coded inapplicable for the presence of an enlarged lateral depression (Balanoff et al., 2009).

6. The interfenestral crest of Incisivosaurus is recessed (Balanoff et al., 2009).

7. Incisivosaurus lacks a subotic recess (Balanoff et al., 2009).

8. As Balanoff et al. (2009) state the boundary between the basisaphenoid and basioccipital is "not well defined due to the high degree of fusion of the braincase as well as a fracture that runs transversely through this region", Incisivosaurus is recoded as having a basisphenoid recess of uncertain position.

9. Incisivosaurus lacks an inflated parasphenoid (Balanoff et al., 2009).

12. Incisivosaurus has hollow basipterygoid processes (Balanoff et al., 2009).

13. Incisivosaurus has a shallow dorsal tympanic recess (Balanoff et al., 2009).

14. Incisivosaurus lacks an accessory recess dorsal to the crista interfenestralis (Balanoff et al., 2009).

15. Incisivosaurus has a posterior tympanic recess (Balanoff et al., 2009), but it's lateral exit is of unknown position.

17. Incisivosaurus has a V-shaped premaxillary symphysis (Balanoff et al., 2009).

21. Incisivosaurus has a promaxillary fenestra (maxillary fenestra of Balanoff et al., 2009).

23. Incisivosaurus only has one nasal fossa (Balanoff et al., 2009), so cannot be said to have "extensive pneumatic fossae".

29. Incisivosaurus does not preserve the jugal-quadratojugal contact (Balanoff et al., 2009).

30. Incisivosaurus has a lateral lacrimal expansion above the orbit (Balanoff et al., 2009).

31. Incisivosaurus has a lacrimal foramen (Balanoff et al., 2009).

33. Incisivosaurus lacks a prefrontal (Balanoff et al., 2009).

34. Incisivosaurus has a transverse nasofrontal suture (Balanoff et al., 2009).

40. Incisivosaurus lacks an inclined quadrate (Balanoff et al., 2009).

44. Incisivosaurus lacks short paroccipital processes (Balanoff et al., 2009).

49. Incisivosaurus has a suborbital fenestra larger than 25% orbital height (Xu et al., 2002).

51. Incisivosaurus has a prominent coronoid process on its surangular (Balanoff et al., 2009).

58. Incisivosaurus lacks a medial/dorsal articular process (Xu et al., 2002).

60. Incisivosaurus has a convex caenagnathoid-like mandibular articulation (Xu et al., 2002).

64. Incisivosaurus has only nine dentary teeth (Balanoff et al., 2009).

69. Incisivosaurus lacks distinct interdental plates (Xu et al., 2002).

70. Incisivosaurus is polymorphic, as the first premaxillary tooth has a flat lingual side while the second is oval in section (Balanoff et al., 2009).

176. The anterior frontal edge underlying the nasal cannot be seen in Incisivosaurus (Balanoff et al., 2009), so it cannot be coded for the presence of a notch.

179. Incisivosaurus has a non-triangular dentary (Xu et al., 2002).

180. The prearticular is indistinguishable from the angular in Incisivosaurus (Balanoff et al., 2009), making the internal mandibular fenestra impossible to define.

182. Incisivosaurus' naris overlaps its antorbital fossa (Balanoff et al., 2009).

184. Incisivosaurus has a basisphenoid recess divided by a bar of bone (Balanoff et al., 2009).

186. Incisivosaurus lacks basipterygoid recesses (Balanoff et al., 2009).

187. Incisivosaurus has a posteriorly placed maxillary fenestra, as I identify the posterodorsal fenestra as this.

193. Incisivosaurus lacks a dorsally curved anterior postorbital process (Balanoff et al., 2009).

197. Incisivosaurus does not have a decurved dentary (Balanoff et al., 2009).

199. Incisivosaurus has a flattened internarial bar (Balanoff et al., 2009).

 

Calvo et al., 2004 on Unenlagia paynemili

142. Unenlagia paynemili lacks a lateral ridsge on its deltopectoral crest (Calvo et al., 2004).

152. The supposed pedal ungual of Unenlagia paynemili is probably a manual ungual due to the enlarged flexor tubercle and dorsal margin which arches high over the proximal surface, and is strongly curved (Calvo et al., 2004).

158. Unenlagia paynemili lacks a supracetabular crest (Calvo et al., 2004).

159. Unenlagia paynemili has a supratrochanteric process (Calvo et al., 2004).

163. Unenlagia paynemili has a prominent antitrochanter (Calvo et al., 2004).

176. As the pubis of Unenlagia paynemili lacks most of the articular surface and is disarticulated, its orientation is unknown.

177. Unenlagia paynemili has an anterior pubic boot (Calvo et al., 2004).

179. Calvo et al. added a new state for taxa with posteriorly concave pubes, but do not state which taxa they code this way besides the two Unenlagia species. Sinornithosaurus (Xu et al., 1999) and Confuciusornis (Goernemann, 1999) have this state as well though. The character is ordered.

 

Makovicky et al., 2003 on Byronosaurus and Ji et al., 2003 on Shenzhousaurus

The same matrix is used for both of these papers, with 220 characters and 50 taxa. They found 432 mpts with a CI of 0.45, but the matrix or character list was never published or made available online. Based on the cladogram, Shenzhousaurus orientalis ("unnamed toothed ornithomimid" in Makovicky et al.), Archaeornithomimus asiaticus, Ornithomimus edmontonicus, Anserimimus planinychus and IGM 100/44 (as EK troodontid) were added from Xu et al.'s (2002) Sinovenator matrix, while Sinraptor dongi was excluded. Based on the character list of Hwang et al. (2004), the added characters were 208-222 of the latter study. Still, since none of the data were made available for either 2003 analysis, the new taxa and characters are dealt with below.

 

Hwang et al., 2004 on Huaxiagnathus

Taxon issues-

Citipati osmolskae- In almost all future versions of the matrix and in the 2003 versions noted above, this is used for the data previously ascribed to IGM 100/42. As the specimens are probably from different taxa, Citipati is here coded separately.
EK troodontid- This is IGM 00/44.
Liaoning ornithomimid- This is Shenzhousaurus orientalis, named five months earlier.
Ornithomimus edmonticus- A misspelling of Ornithomimus edmontonicus, this has more recently been synonymized with Dromiceiomimus brevitertius which has priority (see entry). D. samueli is also used for coding here.

Oddly, the newly added ornithomimosaurs and IGM 100/44 are coded inapplicable for most characters for which their states are unknown. Thus inapplicable is not corrected below for these taxa when the state is actually unknown.

1. Sinosauropteryx does not have remiges (Currie and Chen, 2001), so should be coded inapplicable. Sinornithosaurus does not preserve remiges (Xu et al., 2001), so should be coded unknown.

2. Shenzhousaurus (Ji et al., 2003) has a round orbit.

3. Huaxiagnathus does not preserve the anteroventral postorbital, so the presence of an orbital process is unknown (Hwang et al., 2004).

4. Sinosauropteryx (Currie and Chen, 2001) and Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006) lack an upcurved anterior postorbital process. Dromiceiomimus (Makovicky et al., 2004) has an uncurved anterior postorbital process.

5. Garudimimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005) lacks a constricted laterotemporal fenestra. The postorbital of Huaxiagnathus is too poorly preserved to code (Hwang et al., 2004).

6. Clark et al. (2002) note the "fenestrae ovale and rotundum cannot be identified within" the otic recess, so the structure of the interfenestral crest is unknown in Citipati.

8. The states in this are switched from prior versions. Erlikosaurus (Perle, 1981), Citipati (Digimorph) and Archaeopteryx (Elzanowski and Wellnhoffer, 1996) have a subotic recess. Gorgosaurus, Shuvuuia and Mononykus are corrected from prior versions.

10. Citipati (Digimorph) has an undivided basisphenoid recess.

11. Compsognathus (Ostrom, 1978) lacks an inflated cultriform process. Dromiceiomimus (Tahara and Larsson, 2011) and Byronosaurus (Bever and Norell, 2009) have an inflated cultriform process.

12. Citipati (Clark et al., 2002) should be coded inapplicable due to its reduced basipterygoid processes.

13. Compsognathus (Ostrom, 1978) has unreduced basipterygoid processes.

15. Citipati (Clark et al., 2002) should be coded inapplicable due to its reduced basipterygoid processes.

16. Chirostenotes (Sues, 1997) lacks a dorsal tympanic recess. Allosaurus (Chure, 2000) and Shenzhousaurus (Ji et al., 2003) have a shallow dorsal tympanic recess. Conchoraptor is polymorphic, with both a shallow (coding in Hwang et al., 2004) and deep recess (Kundrat and Janecek, 2007).

17. IGM 100/44 (Makovicky and Norell, 2004) lacks an accessory pneumatic recess dorsal to the otic recess.

20. Huaxiagnathus (Hwang et al., 2004) and Citipati (Clark et al., 2002) have a premaxilla subnarial process which extends posterior to the naris. Compsognathus' process doesn't extend posterior to the naris, but whether it contacts the nasal is unknown (Ostrom, 1978; Peyer, 2006).

21. Incisivosaurus has a flattened internarial bar (Balanoff et al., 2009).

22. Compsognathus (Ostrom, 1978) lacks a crenulated ventral premaxillary margin.

23. Compsognathus (Ostrom, 1978), Sinosauropteryx (Currie and Chen, 2001) and Huaxiagnathus (Hwang et al., 2004) have nares completely anterior to their antorbital fossa. Citipati (Clark et al., 2002) has a naris which overlaps its antorbital fossa. Byronosaurus is corrected.

24. Gallimimus (Osmolska et al., 1972) has a U-shaped premaxillary symphysis. Garudimimus is corrected.

25. Shenzhousaurus' maxillary palatal shelf is hidden behind the medial antorbital fossa wall so cannot be coded (Ji et al., 2003).

26. Sinosauropteryx (Currie and Chen, 2001) and Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006) lack a maxillary tooth-like process.

27. Gallimimus is corrected.

28. Huaxiagnathus (Hwang et al., 2004), Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006) and Citipati (Clark et al., 2002) have a posteriorly placed maxillary fenestra.

29. Shenzhousaurus (Ji et al., 2003) lack a promaxillary fenestra. Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006), Gallimimus (Osmolska et al., 1972) and Citipati (Clark et al., 2002) have a promaxillary fenestra.

30. Shenzhousaurus (Ji et al., 2003) and Dromiceiomimus (Rauhut, 2003) have a sharp rim around the antorbital fossa. Citipati (Digimorph) is polymorphic. Allosaurus and Oviraptor are corrected. All taxa below Citipati and above Incisivosaurus in the matrix seem to have been miscoded as unknown, including 18 taxa that should be coded and were in earlier versions.

31. Huaxiagnathus (Hwang et al., 2004), Sinosauropteryx (Currie and Chen, 2001) and Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006) lack highly pneumatized nasals.

32. As the only previously derived taxa (Struthiomimus and Gallimimus) were incorrectly changed to be plesiomorphic, this character no longer varies in Hwang et al.'s matrix. Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006) have a long dorsal jugal process. Ornithomimus is polymorphic, as some specimens have a short process (Russell, 1972). Huaxiagnathus (Hwang et al., 2004) and Sinosauropteryx (Currie and Chen, 2001) are too poorly preserved to code.

33. Huaxiagnathus (Hwang et al., 2004; based on height), Sinosauropteryx (Currie and Chen, 2001; based on height) and Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006) have a strap-like posterior jugal process. Dromiceiomimus (coding in Kobayashi, 2004) and Archaeopteryx (Elzanowski and Wellnhofer, 1996) have a rod-like posterior jugal process.

36. Gallimimus is corrected.

37. Huaxiagnathus (Hwang et al., 2004) has an unfused jugal and quadratojugal.

38. Gallimimus (Osmolska et al., 1972) and Citipati (Clark et al., 2002) have a lateral lacrimal horn. Dromiceiomimus is polymorphic, as some specimens (Russell, 1972) have a lateral horn. Huaxiagnathus (Hwang et al., 2004) does not preserve the dorsal lacrimal, so cannot be coded.

39. Dromiceiomimus is polymorphic, as some specimens (Tahara and Larsson, 2011) have a pneumatic lacrimal.

40. Garudimimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005), Gallimimus (Osmolska et al., 1987), Struthiomimus (Sereno, 2001), Ornithomimus (Makovicky et al., 2004) and Citipati (Clark et al., 2002) have elongate posterodorsal lacrimal processes. Sinosauropteryx does not preserve a complete anterodorsal process (Currie and Chen, 2001), so must be coded 0/2.

41. Sinosauropteryx (Currie and Chen, 2001) and Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006) have a reduced prefrontal. Shenzhousaurus (Ji et al., 2003) has a prefrontal based on articular surfaces on the lacrimal and frontal, but its size is unknown.

42. Huaxiagnathus has a nasofrontal suture >60 degrees (Hwang et al., 2004), using the width of the left frontal and the posterior extent of the suture of the right one. Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006) also has a transverse suture.

44. Huaxiagnathus (Hwang et al., 2004), Sinosauropteryx (Currie and Chen, 2001) and Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006) have a gently curved orbital process on their frontal.

45. Citipati's nasal articular surface of its frontal is hidden (Clark et al., 2002), so cannot be coded.

46. Huaxiagnathus (Hwang et al., 2004) and Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006) lack a parietal sagittal crest.

47. Compsognathus (Ostrom, 1978; Peyer, 2006) has unfused parietals. Confuciusornis is corrected.

50. Sinosauropteryx (Currie and Chen, 2001) lacks a lateral squamosal shelf. Shenzhousaurus (Ji et al., 2003) has one.

51. Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006) and IGM 100/44 (Barsbold et al., 1987) have a single-headed quadrate.

52. Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006) has a non-inclined quadrate. Dromiceiomimus is polymorphic, as some specimens (Russell, 1972) are not inclined over 105 degrees.

53. Dromiceiomimus (Tahara and Larsson, 2011) has a pneumatic quadrate.

54. Citipati (Clark et al., 2002) and IGM 100/44 (Barsbold et al., 1987) have a narrow dorsal quadrate tab. Sinosauropteryx cannot be measured from Currie and Chen's (2001) figure, as the medial extent of the paraquadrate foramen is not clear, nor is the lateral extent of the dorsal quadrate.

55. Citipati (Clark et al., 2002) and Troodon (Currie and Zhao, 1994) have a tall foramen magnum.

57. Sinosauropteryx (Currie and Chen, 2001) has a slender paroccipital process.

58. Tsaagan is corrected.

60. Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006) and Dromiceiomimus (Tahara and Larsson, 2011) have a ventral ectopterygoid fossa.

62. Compsognathus (Ostrom, 1978), Dromiceiomimus (Parks, 1928) and Citipati (Clark et al., 2002) have an unreduced anterior pterygoid flange.

64. Whether the jugal process is absent in Shenzhousaurus is unknown, as the preserved posterior process is the pterygoid process (Ji et al., 2003).

65. Shenzhousaurus (Ji et al., 2003) has a large suborbital fenestra.

66. Dromiceiomimus (Tahara and Larsson, 2011) has a slightly medially inflected dentary symphysis. The state in Sinosauropteryx cannot be coded from the figures in Currie and Chen (2001).

67. Shenzhousaurus (Ji et al., 2003) lacks a decurved dentary. Harpymimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005) has a decurved dentary. Dromiceiomimus is polymorphic, as some specimens (Makovicky et al., 2004) have decurved dentaries.

68. Sinosauropteryx (coding in Senter, 2007) lacks a strong coronoid eminence.

69. Shenzhousaurus (Ji et al., 2003) and Dromiceiomimus (Makovicky et al., 2004) have a short posterodorsal dentary process. Compsognathus (Ostrom, 1978) has a small notch in the posterior dentary as preserved, which may be the posterodorsal process, but without an external mandibular fenestra this is difficult to judge. Any process is not large though, so it is coded 0/1 here. The posterior mandible of Huaxiagnathus (Hwang et al., 2004) is too poorly preserved to code.

70. The presence of a lateral dentary ridge in Sinosauropteryx cannot be coded from the figures in Currie and Chen (2001).

71. Citipati (Clark et al., 2002) has a triangular dentary. Dromiceiomimus (Makovicky et al., 2004) has subparallel dorsal and ventral dentary edges.

73. IGM 100/44 (Barsbold et al., 1987) lacks a surangular spine. Huaxiagnathus (Hwang et al., 2004), Sinosauropteryx (Currie and Chen, 2001) and Compsognathus (Ostrom, 1978; Peyer, 2006) lack an external mandibular fenestra, so should be coded inapplicable. The posterior edge of Shenzhousaurus' external mandibular fenestra is hidden (Ji et al., 2003), so the presence of a surangular spine is unknown.

74. Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006) lacks a large internal mandibular fenestra.

75. Dromiceiomimus is polymorphic, as some specimens (Kobayashi, 2004) lack a posterior surangular foramen. Gallimimus is corrected.

76. Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006) lacks a widely laterally exposed splenial.

77. Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006) has a coronoid, but of unknown size. Archaeopteryx is corrected.

78. Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006) lacks a mediodorsal articular process.

79. Huaxiagnathus (Hwang et al., 2004) and Sinosauropteryx (Currie and Chen, 2001) have a short retroarticular process. Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006) has an elongate retroarticular process.

80. Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006) and Shenzhousaurus (Ji et al., 2003) have a plesiomorphic short mandibular glenoid.

82. Compsognathus (Ostrom, 1978) has a second premaxillary tooth much larger than the third.

84. IGM 100/44 only has distal serrations on its dentary teeth (Barsbold et al., 1987).

85. Shenzhousaurus (Ji et al., 2003) has less than twenty-five dentary teeth.

86. Sinosauropteryx (Currie and Chen, 2001) and IGM 100/44 (Barsbold et al., 1987) have large serrations.

88. Compsognathus is polymorphic, as a few teeth have constricted bases (Rauhut, 2003).

89. Shenzhousaurus (Ji et al., 2003) lacks smaller and closely packed anterior dentary teeth.

90. Dromiceiomimus is oddly coded 0, while other toothless taxa are coded inapplicable. Sinosauropteryx (coding in Azuma and Currie, 2000) has unfused interdental plates.

93. Huaxiagnathus (Hwang et al., 2004), Sinosauropteryx (Currie and Chen, 2001) and Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006) lack overhanging anterior cervical epipophyses.

94. IGM 100/44 (Barsbold et al., 1987) has a transversely compressed axial neural spine.

95. Dromiceiomimus (Makovicky et al., 2004) and IGM 100/44 (Barsbold et al., 1987) have distally placed epipophyses.

96. Huaxiagnathus (Hwang et al., 2004) and Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006) have anterior cervical centra completely below the neural arch. Anserimimus (Bronowicz, 2011) has anterior cervical centra extending posteriorly past the neural arch. Sinosauropteryx (Currie and Chen, 2001) is polymorphic. Archaeornithomimus (pers. obs.) cannot be coded, as no cervicals anterior to the fifth are known.

97. Anserimimus (Bronowicz, 2011) lacks carotid processes. Dromiceiomimus (Makovicky, 1995) has carotid processes.

98. Archaeornithomimus (pers. obs.) cannot be coded, as no cervicals anterior to the fifth are known and the fifth is only 30% wider than tall.

99. Huaxiagnathus (Hwang et al., 2004) and IGM 100/44 (Barsbold et al., 1987) have anteroposteriorly long anterior cervical neural spines. Sinosauropteryx (Currie and Chen, 2001) is polymorphic.

100. Gorgosaurus (Britt, 1993) is polymorphic, as some cervicals have two pairs of pleurocoels.

101. Anserimimus (Bronowicz, 2011) lacks opisthocoelous cervicals. Compsognathus (Ostrom, 1978; Peyer, 2006) has opisthocoelous cervicals. Shenzhousaurus (Ji et al., 2003) does not preserve cervicals or the first few dorsals, so cannot be coded.

102. Compsognathus (Ostrom, 1978; Peyer, 2006) and Anserimimus (Bronowicz, 2011) lack large anterior dorsal hypapophyses.

103. Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006) and Anserimimus (coding in Kobayashi, 2004) lack stalked dorsal parapophyses. Utahraptor is corrected.

104. Anserimimus (coding in Kobayashi, 2004) has hyposphene-hypantra.

106. Sinosauropteryx (Currie and Chen, 2001) and Anserimimus (Bronowicz, 2011) have some non-pleurocoelous dorsal centra.

107. Archaeornithomimus and Dromiceiomimus are provisionally coded unknown for anterior dorsal transverse process length until it can be verified.

108. Anserimimus (coding in Kobayashi, 2004) lacks dorsal neural spine tables.

109. Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006) and Anserimimus (coding in Kobayashi, 2004) have apically extensive ligament scars on their dorsal neural spines.

110. Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006) has five sacral vertebrae. Harpymimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005), Anserimimus (coding in Kobayashi, 2004) and Deinonychus (Ostrom, 1976) have six sacrals. Conchoraptor is scored as nonexistant state 3, but has more than six sacrals (coding in Lu, 2004).

112. Anserimimus (coding in Kobayashi, 2004) has ventrally flattened/grooved posterior sacrals.

113. Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006) and Anserimimus (coding in Kobayashi, 2004) lack sacral pleurocoels. Shenzhousaurus (Ji et al., 2003) lacks pleurocoels on some sacrals at least.

114. Anserimimus (coding in Kobayashi, 2004) lacks a procoelous posterior sacrum.

115. Anserimimus (Kobayashi, 2004) has a caudal transition point.

116. Anserimimus (Kobayashi, 2004) has more than ten caudals with traverse processes.

117. Sinosauropteryx (coding in Rauhut, 2003), Compsognathus (coding in Rauhut, 2003) and Anserimimus (Bronowicz, 2011) have oval proximal caudal central articular surfaces.

118. Anserimimus (coding in Kobayashi, 2004) lacks accessory mid caudal neural spines. Compsognathus (Ostrom, 1978; Peyer, 2006) is polymorphic. Archaeornithomimus (pers. obs. of AMNH 21791) has neural arches which are too poorly preserved to code.

119. Anserimimus (coding in Kobayashi, 2004) has neural spines on its distal caudals. The condition in Sinosauropteryx cannot be determined from Currie and Chen (2001).

120. Huaxiagnathus (Hwang et al., 2004), Sinosauropteryx (Currie and Chen, 2001) and Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006) have short distal caudal prezygapophyses. Anserimimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005) has moderately long prezygapophyses.

121. Anserimimus (coding in Kobayashi, 2004) has between 25 and 40 caudals. Huaxiagnathus (Hwang et al., 2004), Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006) and Archaeornithomimus (pers. obs. of AMNH 21791-21793) have more than twenty-five caudal vertebrae at least, but whether they had over forty is unknown.

122. Huaxiagnathus (Hwang et al., 2004), Sinosauropteryx (Currie and Chen, 2001), Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006) and Anserimimus (unpublished photo) lack dorsally broad proximal chevrons. Archaeornithomimus (pers. obs.) does not preserve chevrons. Gallimimus and Struthiomimus are corrected.

123. This character is modified to include a third state- bifurcate at both ends. It should be ordered. Zanabazar (Norell et al., 2009) has chevrons with both anterior and posterior bifurcation. Deinonychus (Ostrom, 1969) only has some chevrons with posterior bifurcation, so should be coded 1+2. The condition in Sinosauropteryx (Currie and Chen, 2001) and Compsognathus (Ostrom, 1978; Peyer, 2006) cannot be determined from the literature Hwang et al. used.

124. Citipati (Clark et al., 2002) has long cervical ribs. Sinosauropteryx (Currie and Chen, 2001) is polymorphic.

125. Anserimimus (coding in Kobayashi, 2004) lacks ossified uncinate processes.

126. Huaxiagnathus (Hwang et al., 2004), Sinosauropteryx (Currie and Chen, 2001), Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006) and Anserimimus (coding in Kobayashi, 2004) lack ossified sternal ribs.

127. The medial gastralia are longer in Huaxiagnathus (Hwang et al., 2004), Sinosauropteryx (Currie and Chen, 2001) and Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006). The lateral gastralia are longer in Shenzhousaurus (Ji et al., 2003).

128. Huaxiagnathus (Hwang et al., 2004), Sinosauropteryx (Currie and Chen, 2001) and Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006) are coded inapplicable.

129. Huaxiagnathus (Hwang et al., 2004), Sinosauropteryx (Currie and Chen, 2001) and Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006) are coded inapplicable.

130. Gorgosaurus, Huaxiagnathus (Hwang et al., 2004), Sinosauropteryx (Currie and Chen, 2001) and Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006) are coded inapplicable.

132. Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006) lacks a hypocleidium.

133. Anserimimus (coding in Kobayashi, 2004) lacks a laterally everted acromion. Compsognathus (Ostrom, 1978; Peyer, 2006) only preserves the acromion as impressions, so cannot be coded. Archaeornithomimus (pers. obs. of AMNH 6567) does not preserve the acromion.

135. Archaeornithomimus (pers. obs. of AMNH 6567), Gallimimus (Osmolska et al., 1972) and Citipati (Nesbitt et al., 2009) have an unfused scapulocoracoid. Anserimimus (Barsbold, 1988) has a fused scapulocoracoid. Dromiceiomimus is polymorphic (Sternberg, 1933; Kobayashi, 2004).

136. As per the elimination of the long posteroventral process state noted above, Archaeornithomimus (pers. obs. of AMNH 6567) and Ornithomimus (Sternberg, 1933) are recoded as having shallow coracoids. Anserimimus (coding in Kobayashi, 2004) also has a shallow coracoid.

137. Anserimimus (coding in Kobayashi, 2004) lacks an inflected coracoid. Archaeornithomimus (pers. obs. of AMNH 6567) has an inflected coracoid. The condition in Sinosauropteryx (Currie and Chen, 2001) and Compsognathus (Ostrom, 1978; Peyer, 2006) cannot be determined from the literature Hwang et al. used.

138. Citipati (Nesbitt et al., 2009) lacks a laterally facing glenoid. Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006) and Dromiceiomimus (Sternberg, 1933) have a laterally facing glenoid.

139. Anserimimus (unpublished photo) has a humerus shorter than the scapula. Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006) has a humerus longer than the scapula. Dromiceiomimus is polymorphic, as some specimens (Parks, 1933) have a humerus longer than their scapula.

140. Anserimimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2006) has a sharply angled deltopectoral crest, so is recoded 1. Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006) has a low angled crest.

141. Huaxiagnathus (Hwang et al., 2004), Sinosauropteryx (Currie and Chen, 2001) and Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006) lack a lateral ridge on the deltopectoral crest. Anserimimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2006) has a ridge.

142. Sinosauropteryx (Currie and Chen, 2001), Compsognathus (Ostrom, 1978; Peyer, 2006) and Anserimimus (unpublished photo) have a short olecranon.

143. Anserimimus (coding in Kobayashi, 2004) lacks a strongly curved distal ulnar surface. Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006) has a strongly curved edge. Huaxiagnathus (Hwang et al., 2004) cannot be coded, as the ulnae are preserved in lateral/medial view and mostly embedded in the slab.

144. Sinosauropteryx (Currie and Chen, 2001) and Anserimimus (coding in Kobayashi, 2004) lack a divided ulnar cotyle.

145. Dromiceiomimus preserves a supposed ulnare in ROM 840 which cannot be observed in the figure (Parks, 1928), but since only two carpals are mentioned, they are likely to be distal carpals I and II. Undescribed specimen RTMP 95.110.1 definitely preserves an ulnare (Kobayashi, 2004), which is triangular in extensor view. It is here left unknown. Anserimimus (Barsbold, 1988) only preserves distal carpals I and II, so cannot be coded for ulnare shape.

148. Dromiceiomimus (Kobayashi, 2004) and IGM 100/44 (Barsbold et al., 1987) have a large semilunate carpal. Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006) and Anserimimus (Kobayashi, 2004) have a small semilunate carpal. Archaeornithomimus (pers. obs.) does not preserve carpals, so cannot be coded.

149. Hwang et al. changed the states from the previous version, combining the states for half the length of metacarpal II and less than half the length of metacarpal II, and adding a new state "very short and wider transversely than long proximodistally". Yet this is a composite character now, since metacarpal proportions vary independently of length. Indeed, the only taxa coded this way are parvicursorines, of which at least Mononykus would also have the state "subequal in length to metacarpal II". This character is retained as only coding for metacarpal I length, not proportions. Sinosauropteryx (Currie and Chen, 2001) and Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006; Gishlick and Gauthier, 2007) have metacarpal I much shorter than metacarpal II. Shenzhousaurus (Ji et al., 2003) cannot be coded, as the proportion of digit I consisting of metacarpal I is unknown.

150. Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006) has phalanges on manual digit III.

151. Hwang et al. add an additional state for straight manual unguals. The character should be ordered. Manual ungual I of Archaeornithomimus (pers. obs. of AMNH 6576) is highly curved. Shenzhousaurus' manual ungual I is too incomplete to precisely code for curvature, though it is not straight (Ji et al., 2003).

153. Sinosauropteryx (Currie and Chen, 2001) and Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006) lack a proximodorsal lip on manual ungual I.

154. Hwang et al. changed the two taxa coded as having very strongly hooked pracetabular processes to only having moderately hooked processes, as in my discussion above, but did not change their character list to reflect the loss of state 2. Sinosauropteryx (Currie and Chen, 2001), Ornitholestes (pers. obs.), Shenzhousaurus (Ji et al., 2003), Caudipteryx (Zhou et al., 2000), and Rinchenia (unpublished photo) have a large hook. Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006) has a low or absent hook. Conchoraptor was changed to have a low or absent hook, but since other oviraptorids have a large hook and Hwang et al.'s other coding changes to this character are all incorrect, it is provisionally retained as having a large hook here (the ilium has never been illustrated). Mononykus cannot be coded, as the preacetabular process is almost entirely missing (Perle et al., 1994). Chirostenotes cannot be coded, as the preacetabular process is broken anteriorly (Currie and Russell, 1988).

155. Archaeornithomimus (Hutchinson, 2001) has a short preacetabular process.

156. Dromiceiomimus (Parks, 1933) has a posteriorly sloped anterior edge. Huaxiagnathus (Hwang et al., 2004) and Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006) have a strongly rounded anterior edge. Archaeornithomimus (Hutchinson, 2001) lacks a sloped edge at least. Based on an unpublished photo, Anserimimus' anterior edge is either strongly rounded or sloped.

157. The illustration in Currie and Chen (2001) is not sufficient to code Sinosauropteryx as lacking a supracetabular crest. Huaxiagnathus seems to have a crest (Hwang et al., 2004), though its development is uncertain.

158. Huaxiagnathus (Hwang et al., 2004), Sinosauropteryx (Currie and Chen, 2001) and Shenzhousaurus (Ji et al., 2003) lack a pointed postacetabular process. Sinornithosaurus (Xu et al., 1999) has a pointed postacetabular process. Archaeornithomimus (Hutchinson, 2001) cannot be coded, as most of the dorsal blade is missing. Dromaeosaurus does not preserve pelvic material (Colbert and Russell, 1969). Achillobator is corrected.

159. Dromiceiomimus (codinbg in Kobayashi, 2004) and Anserimimus (coding in Kobayashi, 2004) have divergent postacetabular processes. Archaeornithomimus (Hutchinson, 2001) cannot be coded, as most of the dorsal blade is missing.

160. Sinosauropteryx (Currie and Chen, 2001) lacks a supratrochanteric process.

161. Shuvuuia (coding in Longrich and Currie, 2009) has a shallow to absent brevis fossa.

162. Archaeornithomimus (Smith and Galton, 1990) and Dromiceiomimus (Hutchinson, 2001) have low antitrochanters.

163. Rahonavis (Forster et al., 1998) has a posteriorly extensive cuppedicus fossa. Sinosauropteryx (Currie and Chen, 2001) and Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006) have a cuppedicus fossa which is anteriorly limited.

164. Shenzhousaurus (Ji et al., 2003) and Rahonavis (unpublished photos) have a deep cuppedicus fossa. Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006) has a shallow cuppedicus fossa. Sinosauropteryx (Currie and Chen, 2001) has a cuppedicus fossa, but the degree of lateral overhang is uncertain.

165. Shenzhousaurus (Ji et al., 2003) has a proximodorsal ischial process. Archaeornithomimus is polymorphic (pers. obs. of AMNH 6558).

166. Huaxiagnathus (Hwang et al., 2004) has a decurved ischial shaft. Dromiceiomimus is polymorphic (Parks, 1933). Harpymimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005) does not preserve the ischial shaft, so cannot be coded.

171. Anserimimus (unpublished photo) has a long ischium. Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006) has a short ischium.

172. Anserimimus (coding in Kobayashi, 2004) and Citipati (Clark et al., 1999) have an ischial symphysis. Sinosauropteryx (Currie and Chen, 2001) and Compsognathus (Ostrom, 1978) have ischia which contact but do not join tightly in a symphysis. Harpymimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005) does not preserve the ischial shaft, so cannot be coded.

173. Harpymimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005) does not preserve the ischial shaft, so cannot be coded. Ornitholestes is corrected.

174. Huaxiagnathus (Hwang et al., 2004), Sinosauropteryx (Currie and Chen, 2001) and Archaeornithomimus (pers. obs. of AMNH 6558) lack an obturator tuberosity. Shenzhousaurus' proximoventral ischium is too poorly preserved to determine it it had an obturator tuberosity (Ji et al., 2003).

175. Hwang et al. (2004) add a fourth state "pubis fully posteriorly oriented (opisthopubic)" only for Confuciusornis, but that taxon has a less retroverted pubis than most other taxa coded as having their "pubis moderately posteriorly oriented" (Shuvuuia, Mononykus, Segnosaurus, Velociraptor). Thus the opisthopubic state is not divided further here. Shenzhousaurus (Ji et al., 2003), Anserimimus (unpublished photo), Saurornithoides (Norell et al., 2009), Sinornithosaurus (Xu et al., 1999), Unenlagia (Novas and Puerta, 1997), Rahonavis (Forster et al., 1998) and Archaeopteryx (Wellnhofer, 1993) are mesopubic. Utahraptor does not have reported pubic material, so is left uncoded here pending Britt et al.'s description of the new remains. Garudimimus is corrected.

176. Sinosauropteryx (Currie and Chen, 2001) and Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006) have an anterior pubic boot. Utahraptor does not have reported pubic material, so is left uncoded here pending Britt et al.'s description of the new remains.

177. Citipati (Clark et al., 1999) has a pubic apron emerging from the middle of the shaft. Anserimimus (coding in Kobayashi, 2004) has a pubic apron emerging from the anterior shaft.

178. Chirostenotes (Sues, 1997) has a straight pubic shaft. Anserimimus (unpublished photo) has an anteriorly concave pubic shaft. Sinosauropteryx is polymorphic, as NGMC 127587 (Currie and Chen, 2001) has an anteriorly concave shaft. Harpymimus and Garudimimus are corrected.

179. Compsognathus (Ostrom, 1978) and Anserimimus (coding in Kobayashi, 2004) have a long pubic apron.

180. Anserimimus (coding in Kobayashi, 2004) lacks a capital ligament fossa.

181. Utahraptor (Britt et al., 2001) is provisionally coded as having an anterior trochanter which is either completely or partially unfused to the greater trochanter (Britt et al., 2001), as opposed to Hwang et al.'s coding it as completely unfused. Anserimimus (coding in Kobayashi, 2004) has a deep groove between the anterior and greater trochanters. Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006) has a shallow groove.

182. Huaxiagnathus (Hwang et al., 2004), Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006) and Anserimimus (Bronowicz, 2011) have an alifiorm anterior trochanter.

183. Sinosauropteryx (Currie and Chen, 2001) and Anserimimus (coding in Kobayashi, 2004) lack a posterior trochanter. Shenzhousaurus (Ji et al., 2003) has a posterior trochanter.

184. Anserimimus (coding in Kobayashi, 2004), Citipati (Norell et al., 2001) and Velociraptor (Norell and Makovicky, 1999) have a fourth trochanter. Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006) lacks a fourth trochanter.

185. Huaxiagnathus (Hwang et al., 2004) and Sinosauropteryx (Currie and Chen, 2001) lack an accessory trochanter. Anserimimus (coding in Kobayashi, 2004) has an accessory trochanter.

186. Archaeornithomimus (pers. obs. of AMNH 21800) lacks a medial epicondyle on the femur. Anserimimus (Bronowicz, 2011) and Citipati (unpublished photo of IGM 100/1004) have a medial epicondyle on the femur.

187. Anserimimus (coding in Kobayashi, 2004) lacks an enclosed popliteal fossa.

188. Anserimimus (coding in Kobayashi, 2004) has fibular-calcaneal contact. The distal end of Huaxiagnathus' fibula seems not to be preserved (Hwang et al., 2004).

189. Sinosauropteryx (Currie and Chen, 2001), Archaeornithomimus (pers. obs. of AMNH 6570) and Anserimimus (coding in Kobayashi, 2004) have a shallow proximomedial fibular fossa. Compsognathus (Ostrom, 1978; Peyer, 2006) has a fossa, but of uncertain depth. Dromiceiomimus is provisionally coded as having either a deep or shallow proximomedial fibular fossa, as Kobayashi (2004) nodes it in the latter way.

191. Anserimimus (coding in Kobayashi, 2004) has a shallow anterior intercondylar groove on the tibiotarsus.

192. Huaxiagnathus (Hwang et al., 2004), Sinosauropteryx (Currie and Chen, 2001), Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006) and Anserimimus (coding in Kobayashi, 2004) lack a medial cnemial crest.

193. Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006) and Anserimimus (Kobayashi, 2004) have a tall astragalar ascending process.

194. Anserimimus (coding in Kobayashi, 2004) has a groove across the base of its astragalar ascending process.

195. Anserimimus (coding in Kobayashi, 2004) has an unfused tibiotarsus. Dromiceiomimus (Parks, 1933) fuses its astragalus and tibia.

197. Chirostenotes (Currie and Russell, 1988) lacks metatarsal fusion. IGM 100/44 (Barsbold et al., 1987) lacks distal fusion at least.

200. Dromiceiomimus is polymorphic, as the holotype (Parks, 1926) has a hyperarctometatarsus.

201. Anserimimus (unpublished photo) and IGM 100/44 have a normal-sized pedal ungual II (Barsbold et al., 1987).

202. Compsognathus (Ostrom, 1978) has a proximally placed metatarsal I. Huaxiagnathus (Hwang et al., 2004) has a distally placed metatarsal I. IGM 100/44 has an articulated metatarsal I (Barsbold et al., 1987), but uncertain metatarsus length, so is coded as having either a mid- or distally placed element. Archaeornithomimus seems to preserve metatarsal I (pers. obs. of AMNH 6576), but its position is uncertain, so it is coded ? here. Whether Anserimimus had metatarsal I is uncertain (coding in Kobayashi, 2004). Garudimimus is corrected.

204. Neither specimen of Compsognathus (Ostrom, 1978; Peyer, 2006) preserves a metatarsal IV in lateral or medial view, so its cross section is unknown using the literature.

205. IGM 100/44 (Barsbold et al., 1987) does not have a particularly robust metatarsal IV.

206. As with many vertebral characters, the apical anteroposterior expansion of dorsal neural spines is affected by intervertebral variation. As most taxa cannot be measured for most vertebrae, many more are probably polymorphic than recognized here. It is here quantified as posterior (6-13) neural spines expanded apocally >115% of minimum anteroposterior length. Caudipteryx (Zhou et al., 2000) lacks expanded spines. Sinraptor (Currie and Zhao, 1994), Allosaurus (Chure, 2000), Ornitholestes (Carpenter et al., 2005), Shenzhousaurus (Ji et al., 2003), Garudimimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005), Dromiceiomimus (unpublished photo of RTMP 95.110.1), Anserimimus (unpublished photo), Mononykus (Perle et al., 1994), Sinovenator (Xu et al., 2002), Microraptor (Hwang et al., 2002), Sinornithosaurus (coding in Xu and Zhang, 2005), Velociraptor (Norell and Makovicky, 1999), Deinonychus (Ostrom, 1969), Achillobator (Perle et al., 1999), Unenlagia (unpublished photos), Rahonavis (Forster et al., 1998) and Confuciusornis (Chiappe et al., 1999) have expanded spines. Gorgosaurus (Lambe, 1917), Tyrannosaurus (Brochu, 2003), Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006; Ostrom, 1978), Harpymimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005) and Archaeopteryx (Wellnhofer, 1974, 1993) are polymorphic. Archaeornithomimus (pers. obs.) and Patagonykus (Novas, 1997) are too poorly preserved to code.

207. Microvenator (pers. obs.) and Conchoraptor (coding in Lu, 2004) have manual phalanx I-1 narrower than their radius. Tyrannosaurus (Brochu, 2003), "Ingenia" (Barsbold et al., 1990), Sinornithoides (Russell and Dong, 1994), Microraptor (Hwang et al., 2002), Deinonychus (Ostrom, 1969) and Achillobator (Perle et al., 1999) have manual phalanx I-1 wider than their radius. Compsognathus is polymorphic, as CNJ79 has a slender phalanx (Peyer, 2006). Contra Hwang et al., poor preservation prevents measuring the exact width of Huaxiagnathus' phalanx, though it is very close to the radius in width. Sinornithosaurus cannot be coded, as the radius is largely overlapped by the ulna (Xu et al., 1999).

208. This is a problematic character as coded, since the taxa coded as derived by Hwang et al. are not those with the most restricted angulars. It is also prone to variation within individuals by 3-5% (e.g. Tyrannosaurus, Ornitholestes, Dromaeosaurus). Quantifying the character to separate those taxa whose angulars don't reach the last 5% of the mandible, Sinraptor (Currie and Zhao, 1994), Sinosauropteryx (Ji et al., 2007), Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006), Ornitholestes (AMNH online), Garudimimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005), Gallimimus (Osmolska et al., 1972; Hurum, 2001), Oviraptor (Clark et al., 2002), Rinchenia (unpublished photo), IGM 100/42 (unpublished photo), "Ingenia" (Barsbold et al., 1990), Sinornithosaurus (Xu and Wu, 2001), Tsaagan (Norell et al., 2006), Velociraptor (Norell et al., 2006), Deinonychus (Paul, unpublished), Dromaeosaurus (Currie, 1995) and Archaeopteryx (Paul, 2002) have the condition. Shenzhousaurus (Ji et al., 2003) has a posteriorly extensive angular. Struthiomimus (Osborn, 1916; Kobayashi, 2004), Dromiceiomimus (Parks, 1928; Makovicky et al., 2004) and Conchoraptor (Osmolska, 1976; Barsbold, 1976) are polymorphic. The angular-surangular suture is unclear in Harpymimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005) and Segnosaurus (Barsbold and Maryanska, 1990), so they cannot be coded. Similarly, Shuvuuia (Chiappe et al., 2002) lacks the anterior dentary. Archaeornithomimus (pers. obs.) does not preserve a mandible. Incisivosaurus (Xu et al., 2002) and Confuciusornis (Chiappe et al., 1999) have fused posterior mandibular elements, so cannot be coded. Sinovenator is provisionally coded unknown as Hwang et al.'s other codings are largely incorrect.

209. Shuvuuia (Chiappe et al., 2002), Erlikosaurus (Clark et al., 1994), Avimimus (Kurzanov, 1985), Rinchenia (unpublished photo), Citipati (Clark et al., 2002), IGM 100/42 (unpublished photos), Conchoraptor (unpublished photos), "Ingenia" (Barsbold et al., 1990), Sinornithosaurus (Xu and Wu, 2001), Tsaagan (Norell et al., 2006), Velociraptor (Norell et al., 2006) and Dromaeosaurus (Currie, 1995) have a lateral surangular ridge at the dorsal edge just anterior to the glenoid. Oviraptor (unpublished photos) is too fragmented in this area to code. Compsognathus cannot be coded from Ostrom's (1978) paper, so is left uncoded. Saurornitholestes is left uncoded based on Hwang et al.'s miscoding of most other dromaeosaurids.

210. This is a composite involving the ginglymoidy of metacarpal I and metacarpal II, so only the former bone is coded here. Compsognathus (Gishlick and Gauthier, 2007), Ornitholestes (unpublished photos), Pelecanimimus (Perez-Moreno et al., 1994), Archaeornithomimus (pers. obs. of AMNG 6569), Avimimus (Tsuihiji et al., 2009), Rinchenia (coding in Lu, 2004; presumably based on the articular surface of phalanx I-1) and Achillobator (Perle et al., 1999; based on phalanx I-1) have a ginglymoid metacarpal I. Sinraptor (Currie and Zhao, 1994) and Oviraptor (unpublished photos) do not preserve metacarpal I, so cannot be coded for the newly restricted character.

211. This character involves the distal syndesmosis or adherence between the radius and ulna in ornithomimosaurs, as first proposed by Nicholls and Russell (1985) in Struthiomimus. In that taxon, the proximal articulation is deeply concave on the ulna and the distal articulations are flattened, which the authors interpreted as indicating syndesmosis, where a ligament joins bones in barely mobile articulation. Yet these articulations in Aves match morphologically, but are not joined by ligaments. Rather, they are capable of sliding motion which enables the wing to fold. Thus the articular surfaces themselves are not evidence of reduced mobility in Struthiomimus. There are two forms of proposed motion between the radius and ulna of theropods. Rotation of the radius causing pronation has been proposed in Microvenator (Makovicky and Sues, 1998; based on the concave distal ulnar facet), Troodon (Russell, 1969; based on the roughly circular proximal radius) and Deinonychus (Ostrom, 1969; based on the slightly concave proximal ulnar facet and supposedly poorly developed articular surfaces). Yet Microvenator and Deinonychus both have trangular proximal radii that did not allow rotation (Gishlick, 2002; Senter, 2006), though the morphology of Troodon requires further study. Thus far, all studied saurischians lack the ability to rotate their radius. The other proposed form of motion is that present in birds where the radius slides distally during flexion of the elbow. Carpenter (2002) argued this was absent in non-avian theropods due to the lack of a well developed incisura radialis for the radius to slide in proximally, which was also the osteological correlate found by Vasquez (1993). Indeed this seems true for some taxa such as Allosaurus (Carpenter, 2002), Tyrannosaurus (Carpenter and Smith, 2001), Ornitholestes (Senter, 2006) and Deinonychus (Senter, 2006; though movement was proposed by Gishlick [2001], this seems to be slight). Yet some maniraptorans such as Oviraptor (Osborn, 1924), Sinornithoides (Currie and Dong, 2001), Microraptor (Xu et al., 2000), Archaeopteryx (Vasquez, 1993) and Confuciusornis (Chiappe et al., 1999) possess the sliding morphology based on articulated specimens, and this is also true in Bambiraptor based on manipulation (Senter, 2006). At least the latter taxon also has a well developed incisura radialis. Segnosaurus (unpublished photo of IGM 100/83) and Khaan (Gishlick, 2002) have a reversed articulation with a concave radius, suggesting another mechanism to obtain the same function. Yet some non-maniraptorans like Coelurus (Gishlick, 2002), Tanycolagreus (Carpenter et al., 2005) and ornithomimosaurs also have a deep incisura radialis, but lack most features of the avian wing-folding mechanism, suggesting the incisura depth may not always indicate a sliding radius. Alvarezsaurids also deserve mention, as the two proximal facets in Patagonykus (Novas, 1997) and sutured connection in parvicursorines (Perle et al., 1994) make them the only theropods which definitely lack any motion between the radius and ulna. Despite frequent claims of syndesmosis in ornithomimosaurs (e.g. Perez-Moreno et al., 1994; Kobayashi, 2004; Makovicky et al. 2009), no feature of their morphology suggesting a stronger radioulnar articulation than more basal coelurosaurs has been described. The character is thus rejected and all 32 scored taxa are recoded unknown.

212. "Ingenia" (Barsbold et al., 1990) and Dromaeosaurus (Currie, 1995) lack a dorsal kink to the anterior dentary. Ornitholestes (AMNH online), Pelecanimimus (Makovicky et al., 2004), Alxasaurus (Russell and Dong, 1994), Segnosaurus (Barsbold and Maryanska, 1990), Erlikosaurus (Clark et al., 1994), Caudipteryx (Zhou et al., 2000), Incisivosaurus (Balanoff et al., 2009) and Microvenator (Makovicky and Sues, 1998) have a kink. Troodon is polymorphic (Currie, 1987). The condition in Shuvuuia is uncertain as the anterior dentary is unpreserved (Chiappe et al., 2002).

213. Harpymimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005), Shenzhousaurus (Ji et al., 2003) and Dromaeosaurus (Currie, 1995) lack laterally visible quadrate heads. Garudimimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005) and Caudipteryx (Zhou et al., 2000) have laterally exposed heads. The condition cannot be determined in Sinornithosaurus due to the poor preservation of the squamosals (Xu and Wu, 2001). Sinosauropteryx is left uncoded as the condition cannot be determined from Currie and Chen's (2001) paper.

214. Garudimimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005), Archaeornithomimus (Smith and Galton, 1990), Gallimimus (Osmolska et al., 1972), Struthiomimus (Osborn, 1916), Dromiceiomimus (Parks, 1926), Anserimimus (unpublished photo), Avimimus (Kurzanov, 1987) and Saurornitholestes (Hutchinson, 2001) have a laterally exposed brevis fossa. Sinosauropteryx (Currie and Chen, 2001), Harpymimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005), Sinovenator (Xu et al., 2002), Troodon (Varricchio et al., 2002) and Adasaurus (Barsbold, 1983) lack lateral exposure. Patagonykyus (Novas, 1997) is too fragmentary to judge the lateral exposure of any brevis fossa.

215. Sinraptor (Currie and Zhao, 1994), Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006), Alvarezsaurus (Bonaparte, 1991), Patagonykus (Novas, 1997), Shuvuuia (pers. obs. of IGM 100/1276), Mononykus (unpublished photo), Caudipteryx (pers. obs. of NGMC 97-9-A), Microvenator (Hutchinson, 2001), Microraptor (Hwang et al., 2002), Deinonychus (Ostrom, 1976) and Unenlagia (unpublished photo) lack a vertical ridge on the proximolateral femur. Garudimimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005), Avimimus (Vickers-Rich et al., 2002), Sinornithoides (Currie and Dong, 2001), Adasaurus (Kim et al., 2005), Achillobator (Perle et al., 1999) and Rahonavis (unpublished photo) have the ridge.

216. Sinraptor (Currie and Zhao, 1994), Allosaurus (Gilmore, 1920), Gorgosaurus (Currie, 2003), Tyrannosaurus (Larson, 2008), Shuvuuia (Sereno, 2001), Caudipteryx (Zhou et al., 2000), Avimimus (Vickers-Rich et al., 2002), IGM 100/42 (unpublished photo), Conchoraptor (Osmolska, 1976), Troodon (Currie, 1985), Tsaagan (Norell et al., 2006), Velociraptor (Barsbold and Osmolska, 1999), Deinonychus (Paul, unpublished) and Dromaeosaurus (Currie, 1995) have a well defined supratemporal fossa on their squamosal. Archaeopteryx's squamosal is only preserved in sagittal cross section (Elzanowski and Wellnhofer,m 1996), so cannot be coded.

217. This character should be ordered.

218. Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006) lacks a strongly projected infraglenoid lip. Tyrannosaurus (Brochu, 2003), Huaxiagnathus (Hwang et al., 2004), Harpymimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005), Shuvuuia (pers. obs. of IGM 100/975), Mononykus (Perle et al., 1994), Segnosaurus (Perle, 1979), Avimimus (Kurzanov, 1981), Chirostenotes (Currie and Russell, 1988), IGM 100/42 (unpublished photo), "Ingenia" (unpublished photo), Sinornithoides (Currie and Dong, 2001), Sinornithosaurus (Xu et al., 1999), Saurornitholestes (Jasinoski, 2003), Tsaagan (Norell et al., 2006), Velociraptor (Norell and Makovicky, 1999), Deinonychus (Ostrom, 1974), Achillobator (Perle et al., 1999), Archaeopteryx (Mayr et al., 2005) and Confuciusornis (Chiappe et al., 1999) have a prominent coracoid glenoid lip. Alvarezsaurus (Bonaparte, 1991) cannot be coded as the posterior coracoid margin is missing. Alxasaurus is coded unknown here, as the full extent of the infraglenoid buttress is hidden by the humerus in Russell and Dong's (1994) figure. Similarly, Sinovenator is left uncoded as its coracoid has only been illustrated in posterior view (Xu et al., 2002), as has Microraptor as the coracoids are only visible in anterior (Hwang et al., 2004) or posterior (Xu et al., 2003) views.

219. Sinosauropteryx (Ji et al., 2007), Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006), Pelecanimimus (Perez-Moreno et al., 1994), Garudimimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005), Gallimimus (Hurum, 2001) and Chirostenotes (Currie et al., 1994) lack an upcurved retroarticular process.

220. Alvarezsaurus (Bonaparte, 1991), Segnosaurus (Perle, 1979), Saurornitholestes (Jasinoski, 2003), Achillobator (Perle et al., 1999), Unenlagia comahuensis (Gianechini and Apesteguia, 2011) and Rahonavis (unpublished photo) lack a supraglenoid buttress flange. Sinosauropteryx (Currie and Chen, 2001), Harpymimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005) and Deinonychus (Ostrom, 1969) have a flange. Oviraptor's scapula is too fractured in the relevent area to determine the presence of a supraglenoid flange (unpublished photo). Microvenator's (Makovicky and Sues, 1998) and Chirostenotes' scapula are unknown.

221. Gorgosaurus (Carr, 1996), Incisivosaurus (Balanoff et al., 2009), Oviraptor (unpublished photo), Rinchenia (coding in Xu and Zhang, 2005), "Ingenia" (coding in Xu and Zhang, 2005) and Archaeopteryx (Alonso et al., 2004) lack a ventral laterosphenoid fossa. Allosaurus (McClelland, 1990) has a ventral laterosphenoid fossa.

222. This character should be defined so that basal tubera which span <165% of the occipital condyle width count as closely placed, to best match Hwang et al.'s coding. It excludes the shape and width of the notch between the tubera, which is covered by character 14 of Xu and Zhang (2005). Garudimimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005) and Shuvuuia (Chiappe et al., 2002) have widely spaced basal tubera. Sinraptor (Currie and Zhao, 1994), Allosaurus (McClelland, 1990), Ornitholestes (pers. obs.), Gallimimus (Osmolska et al., 1972), Dromiceiomimus (Tahara and Larsson, 2011) and Troodon (Currie and Zhao, 1994) have narrowly separated basal tubera. Erlikosaurus lacks basal tubera (Clark et al., 1994), so should be coded inapplicable. Oviraptor (unpublished photos) does not preserve basal tubera. Byronosaurus cannot be coded, as the occipital condyle is missing (Makovicky et al., 2003).

 

Xu and Norell, 2004 on Mei

26. The presence of a tooth-like process on the maxillary palate in Mei is unknown as the area is covered by the mandibles and sediment.

32. While coded inapplicable by Xu and Norell, Mei does have a short dorsal jugal process, so is here coded derived.

36. Mei must be coded inapplicable for quadratojugal shape, as it lacks a dorsal process.

38. Mei is conservatively coded here as lacking a dorsal lacrimal horn, but with unknown lateral projection until better photos are available.

40. Mei has a short posterodorsal lacrimal process, as well as a short anterodorsal one.

45. Mei has an anterolateral notch in its frontal.

52. Mei's quadrate is not anteroventrally inclined.

58. Xu and Norell describe Mei's paroccipital processes as "pendulous", contra their coding.

68. Contra Xu and Norell's coding, the dorsal mandibular margin of Mei is too poorly preserved/exposed to code for a coronoid prominence.

69. Similarly, the presence and length of a posterodorsal dentary process cannot be determined in Mei.

71. The amount of taper to the dentary cannot be determined in Mei as the dorsal margin is unpreserved.

79. Mei seems to have an elongate retroarticular process.

85. The number of dentary teeth in Mei cannot be observed.

89. The placement of Mei's dentary teeth cannot be observed.

96. Cervicals 3 and 4 of Mei appear to have centra which do not extend posteriorly past the neural arch when the posterior articulation is held vertical.

103. Xu and Norell themselves state Mei only has "distinct parapophyses; however, they are not as stalk-like as those in advanced dromaeosaurs (for example, Velociraptor)."

135. Mei lacks a fused scapulocoracoid.

138. Mei's scapular glenoid does not face laterally relative to the blade (unpublished photo).

141. Mei has a lateral ridge on its deltopectoral crest (unpublished photo).

153. Due to dividing this character among unguals, Mei is recoded 0 as it appears to lack a proximodorsal lip on ungual I (Xu and Norell, 2004).

169. As with most other taxa, Mei must have an obturator notch, since it has an obturator process.

175. Mei is mesopubic (Xu and Norell, 2004).

195. Mei has a visible tibiotarsal suture (unpublished photo).

198. Metatarsal II in Mei is not deeply ginglymoid (Xu and Norell, 2004).

199. Metatarsal III is deeply ginglymoid in Mei (coding in Senter, 2007).

201. Mei's second pedal ungual is not >40% larger than ungual II (Xu and Norell, 2004).

202. Mei's metatarsal I is distally placed (Xu and Norell, 2004).

205. Mei's metatarsal IV is not much wider than metatarsal II (Xu and Norell, 2004).

206. Mei lacks dorsally expanded posterior dorsal neural spines (Xu and Norell, 2004).

217. Mei's dentary teeth are not exposed (Xu and Norell, 2004), so their extent cannot be measured.

218. Mei has a deep subglenoid notch on its coracoid (Xu and Norell, 2004).

 

Mayr et al., 2005 on Archaeopteryx

This is a modification of Hwang et al.'s (2002) analysis with eight changed codings for Archaeopteryx, and one for Rahonavis.

28. Archaeopteryx is corrected.

48. Archaeopteryx is corrected.

106. Archaeopteryx is corrected.

111. Archaeopteryx is polymorphic (Petronievics and Woodward, 1917). Rahonavis is corrected.

163. Archaeopteryx is corrected.

166. Archaeopteryx has proximally fused metatarsals when older (Heller, 1959; Wellnhofer, 1992).

170. Mayr et al. added a state for a hyperextendable pedal digit II, but non-enlarged pedal ungual II as in Archaeopteryx. While this is true, here I add hyperextendability as a separate character following Senter (2007). Notably, at least Adasaurus should have also been coded this way by Mayr et al., but was not.

171. Mayr et al. correctly recode Archaeopteryx as having a medially attached metatarsal I, but this is true in all birds as noted above, which is why I only code for proximodistal position for this character.

 

Xu and Zhang, 2005 on Pedopenna

This little used matrix seems to be based on Xu's (2002) thesis, which contained one more character. Both matrices exclude Sinraptor, Tsaagan and IGM 100/42, though Xu and Zhang do use the latter to help code Oviraptor for their new characters. Xu (2002) added Graciliraptor, while Xu and Zhang add Pedopenna, Jeholornis and Epidendrosaurus as well.

1. This character codes for anterior snout depth. Instead of comparing depth at the posterior naris, I use the height 25% down the preorbital snout, since naris size and posterior extent could impact the results. The jugal+orbit height is used as a standard to agree with the other characters. The states which match best with Xu and Zhang's data are- height of preorbital snout one fourth from tip >39% of orbit+jugal height (0); <40% (1). Harpymimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005), Microraptor (Ji, 2002), Saurornitholestes (Currie and Varricchio, 2004) and Achillobator (Perle et al., 1999) have a tall snout. Garudimimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005), Shuvuuia (Sereno, 2001) and Shenzhouraptor (Ji et al., 2003) have a low snout. Struthiomimus (Russell, 1972; Knutsen, 2007), Avimimus (Kurzanov, 1987), Byronosaurus (Makovicky et al., 2003), Sinornithosaurus (Xu and Wu, 2001) and Utahraptor are too poorly preserved to code.

2. This is quantified here as angle between alveolar margin and anterior snout ventral to external naris <60 degrees, based on the description in Xu (2002). Harpymimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005), Avimimus (Kurzanov, 1986), Sinornithoides (Russell and Dong, 1994), Troodon (coding in Senter et al., 2004), Sinornithosaurus (Xu and Wu, 2001) and Archaeopteryx (Wellnhofer, 1992) have blunt snouts. Rinchenia (Barsbold et al., 1990) have sharp snouts. Conchoraptor (Barsbold, 1986; Osmolska, 1976) is polymorphic. Oviraptor (Osborn, 1924), Dromaeosaurus (Currie, 1995) and Scansoriopteryx do not preserve the anterior premaxilla. "Ingenia" is provisionally recoded unknown, pending information from an author with verified snout material.

3. Gallimimus (Witmer lab), Sinornithoides (Russell and Dong, 1994), Byronosaurus (Makovicky et al., 2003), Saurornithoides (pers. obs.), Zanabazar (Norell et al., 2009), Velociraptor (Barsbold and Osmolska, 1999) and Shenzhouraptor (Zhang and Zhou, 2002) have deep premaxillae. Harpymimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005) has shallow premaxillae. Microraptor (Xu et al., 2000; Ji, 2002) is polymorphic. Avimimus (Kurzanov, 1987) cannot be coded due to incompleteness.

4. Archaeopteryx is polymorphic, as some specimens (Berlin- Paul, 2002; Thermopolis- Mayr et al., 2007) lack a diastema. Harpymimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005), Avimimus (Vickers-Rich et al., 2002; Tsuihiji et al., 2008) and Shenzhouraptor (Zhou and Zhang, 2003) are inapplicable as they lack premaxillary and maxillary teeth. The specimens of Byronosaurus (Makovicky et al., 2003; Bever and Norell, 2009) do not preserve complete tooth rows at the premaxilla-maxilla contact.

5. This character (Antorbital fenestra large (0) or small (1) relative to orbit) conflates orbit shape (character 8 in this matrix) and the amount of the antorbital fossa covered by the antorbital fenestra (character 239 in Senter, 2007). Thus it is deleted and all 29 scored taxa are recoded unknown.

6. Pelecanimimus (Perez-Moreno et al., 1994), Harpymimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005), Gallimimus (Osmolska et al., 1972), Incisivosaurus (Balanoff et al., 2009), Oviraptor (unpublished photo), Conchoraptor (Elzanowski, 1999) and Sinornithosaurus (Xu and Wu, 2001) lack a slit-shaped promaxillary fenestra. Allosaurus (Smith and Lisak, 2001), Gorgosaurus (Carr, 1999), Tyrannosaurus (Brochu, 2003), Ornitholestes (pers. obs.) and Saurornitholestes (Currie and Varricchio, 2004) have a slit-shaped promaxillary fenestra. Caudipteryx (Zhou et al., 2000), Chirostenotes (Sues, 1997), Rinchenia (unpublished photo), Byronosaurus (Bever and Norell, 2009) and Troodon (Currie, 1985) lack a promaxillary fenestra so should be inapplicable for its shape. The presence of a promaxillary fenestra is uncertain in Shuvuuia (Chiappe et al., 2002) and Erlikosaurus (Clark et al., 1994) so these should be coded unknown.

7. Harpymimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005), Sinovenator (Xu et al., 2002), Sinornithoides (Russell and Dong, 1994), Shenzhouraptor (Ji et al., 2003) and Confuciusornis (Chiappe et al., 1999) lack depressed nasals. Garudimimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005), Gallimimus (Osmolska et al., 1972), Shuvuuia (Sereno, 2001), Saurornithoides (Norell et al., 2009) and Archaeopteryx (Paul, 2002) have depressed nasals. Ornitholestes' (pers. obs.) and Oviraptor's (Osborn, 1924) nasals don't preserve the dorsal edge.

8. This should be ordered with states switched so that medium-sized nares are intermediate condition. It is here quantified compared to jugal+orbit height as- external naris <49% (0); 49-80% (1); >80% (2), as this best agrees with Xu and Zhang's codings. Incisivosaurus (Balanoff et al., 2009), Rinchenia (unpublished photo), Sinovenator (Xu et al., 2002), Sinornithoides (Russell and Dong, 1994) and Velociraptor (Barsbold and Osmolska, 1999) have a small naris. Harpymimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005), Deinonychus (Paul, unpublished) and Confuciusornis (Chiappe et al., 1999) have a medium-sized naris. Sinornithosaurus' nasal is too fragmented to determine if it had a small or medium naris (Xu and Wu, 2001) so is coded 0/1. Similarly, Shenzhouraptor does not have a small naris at least (Zhou and Zhang, 2003). Avimimus (Tsuihiji et al., 2008 noted the supposed posterior narial edge of Kurzanov was an unrelated fenestra) and Dromaeosaurus (Currie, 1995) cannot be coded.

9. Harpymimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005), Avimimus (Kurzanov, 1985) and Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) have a ventral postorbital process longer than the posterior process. Troodon (Currie, 1985) has a longer posterior process. Caudipteryx is polymorphic, as IVPP V12430 (Zhou et al., 2000) has a longer ventral process. Pelecanimimus (Perez-Moreno et al., 1994), Byronosaurus (Makovicky et al., 2003; Bever and Norell, 2009) and Zanabazar (Norell et al., 2009; a small piece of the posterior tip is missing) are too incomplete to code.

10. Ornitholestes (pers. obs.), Harpymimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005) and Byronosaurus (Bever and Norell, 2009) lack a pit in the supratemporal fossa. Caudipteryx (Zhou et al., 2000) and Saurornitholestes (Currie, 1987) have a pit. Troodon is polymorphic (Currie, 1985), as RTMP 79.8.1 has a pit. Oviraptor (unpublished photos) is too fragmentary to code.

11. Avimimus (Kurzanov, 1985), Zanabazar (Norell et al., 2009), Troodon (Currie, 1985) and Velociraptor (Barsbold and Osmolska, 1999) have narrow parietals. Tyrannosaurus (Brochu, 2003), Ornitholestes (pers. obs.), Harpymimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005), Garudimimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005) and Deinonychus (Paul, unpublished) have wide parietals. Saurornithoides (pers. obs.) is too poorly preserved to code.

12. Garudimimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005), Avimimus (Kurzanov, 1985), Sinovenator (Xu et al., 2002), Zanabazar (Digimorph), Troodon (Currie, 1985) lack a dorsally convex parietal. Ornitholestes (pers. obs.), Shuvuuia (Chiappe et al., 2002), Incisivosaurus (Balanoff et al., 2009), Oviraptor (Clark et al., 2002), Rinchenia (unpublished photo), Conchoraptor (Osmolska, 1976), "Ingenia" (Barsbold, 1983), Adasaurus (unpublished photo), Velociraptor (Barsbold and Osmolska, 1999) have a dorsally convex parietal. Pelecanimimus (Perez-Moreno et al., 1994), Caudipteryx (Ji et al., 1998; Zhou et al., 2000), Saurornithoides (pers. obs.) and Dromaeosaurus (Currie, 1995) are too poorly preserved to code.

13. This is here quantified as a pterygoid process apex located <46% from the ventral end being derived, to agree best with Xu and Zhang's codings. Ornitholestes (AMNH online), Harpymimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005), Garudimimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005), Struthiomimus (Osborn, 1916), Shuvuuia (Chiappe et al., 2002), Erlikosaurus (Clark et al., 1994) and Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) have ventrally placed pterygoid flanges. Incisivosaurus (Balanoff et al., 2009) cannot be coded as the process is fused to the pterygoid. Rinchenia (unpublished photo), Saurornithoides (Norell et al., 2009) are too poorly preserved to code.

14. Ornitholestes (pers. obs.), Garudimimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005), Gallimimus (Witmer lab), Avimimus (Kurzanov, 1985) have a wide, U-shaped notch between the basal tubera. Struthiomimus (Makovicky and Norell, 1998), Byronosaurus (Makovicky et al., 2003) have a narrow, V-shaped notch. Oviraptor (unpublished photos) is too poorly preserved to code. Erlikosaurus is inapplicable as it lacks basal tubera (Clark et al., 1994).

16. This should be ordered and the states redefined so that "moderate in depth" is state 1. It is here quantified as maximum posterior dentary height <15% of length (0); 15-50% (1); >50% (2), which best agrees with Xu and Zhang's coding (subsequent reading of Xu, 2002 indicates it is meant to measure mid-dentary height, and define ratios of <9%; 10-50% and >50%). Segnosaurus (Barsbold and Maryanska, 1990), Velociraptor (Sues, 1977) and Confuciusornis (Chiappe et al., 1999) have a shallow dentary. Chirostenotes (Currie et al., 1994) and Oviraptor (unpublished photos) have a moderate dentary. Avimimus (Kurzanov, 1987) and Deinonychus (Ostrom, 1969) have an uncertain dentary length, but based on the mandibular remains do not have a deep dentary at least.

17. This is a variation of Norell et al.'s (2001) character 79, though it only includes vertical processes so excludes Shuvuuia. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) lacks a vertical articular process. Shenzhouraptor (Zhou and Zhang, 2002) has a process.

18. This is quantified as a DSDI of >1.2. Adasaurus (Currie and Varricchio, 2004) has a low DSDI. Microraptor (Ji, 2002) and Sinornithosaurus (Xu and Wu, 2001) are polymorphic. Ornitholestes is better left unknown, as the presence of mesial serrations is uncertain. Chirostenotes (Currie et al., 1994; Sues, 1997), Microvenator (Makovicky and Sues, 1998), Oviraptor (Clark et al., 2002) should be coded unknown, as they may have teeth in unpreserved elements. Incisivosaurus (Balanoff et al., 2009), Byronosaurus (Makovicky et al., 2003) and Scansoriopteryx (Zhang et al., 2002) are inapplicable as they lack serrations, while Sinornithoides (Currie and Dong, 2001) should be because it lacks mesial serrations. Avimimus (Kurzanov, 1985; Tsuihiji et al., 2008) is inapplicable as it lacks teeth.

19. This character (Trunk long, hindlimb/trunk length ratio less than 2 (0) or trunk short, hindlimb/trunk length ratio more than 2 (1)) is refined to only be compared to the femur, to eliminate confounding signals from differing distal hindlimb proportions. Garudimimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005), Microvenator (Makovicky and Sues, 1998), Rinchenia (unpublished photos), Saurornithoides (Russell, 1969), Adasaurus (unpublished photo), Unenlagia (unpublished photos), Rahonavis (unpublished photos), Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) and Confuciusornis (Chiappe et al., 1999) have a long dorsal column, based on the length of their centra. While Caudipteryx does not preserve a completely exposed dorsal series in any specimen, IVPP V12340 (Zhou et al., 2000) does show an anterior, mid and posterior dorsal centrum. Using these lengths over eleven segments results in a dorsal column comparable in length to eudromaeosaurs. Shuvuuia does not preserve significant dorsal remains (pers. obs.). Oviraptor (Smith, 1992) does not preserve the hindlimb. "Ingenia" lacks a preserved dorsal column in the holotype at least (Psihoyos, 1996). The two measured dorsal vertebrae of Achillobator (Perle et al., 1999) are rather short, so the possibility of a short dorsal column cannot be rejected. Similarly, while Sinornithosaurus preserves two short posterior dorsals (Xu et al., 1999), this is also true in Velociraptor which has a long dorsal column.

20. This character (Dorsal vertebrae proportionately short (0) or long (1)) is refined to only include dorsals 6-13 since centrum proportions vary along the column, and is quantified so that long centra are those over 130% of their height. Garudimimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005), Chirostenotes (Sues, 1997), Rinchenia (unpublished photo), Saurornithoides (Norell et al., 2009), Troodon (Makovicky, 1995), Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) and Confuciusornis (Chiappe et al., 1999) have short dorsal centra. Harpymimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005) and Alvarezsaurus (Bonaparte, 1991) have elongate centra. Byronosaurus (Makovicky et al., 2003) is unknown, as only anterior dorsals are known, which are also comparable in length to some taxa with short posterior dorsals.

21. This is similar to Hwang et al.'s (2004) character 206, though it doesn't specify posterior dorsal neural spines and the coding differs by correctly coding more than just compsognathids as having the character. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) lacks expanded spines. Shuvuuia (pers. obs.) is too poorly preserved to code.

22. This character is written as "Middle sacrals (primary sacrals) subequal to (0) or significantly larger than (1) the other sacrals and anterior caudals", referring to the condition in Sinovenator and Microraptor where middle sacrals are transversely expanded. Yet many other taxa have reduced posterior sacrals, so to match Xu and Zhang's intent better, the character is here refined to "Ancestral sacral centra 1 and/or 2 less than 70% the tranmsverse width of sacral 3". Ornitholestes (unpublished photo), Garudimimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005), Alvarezsaurus (Bonaparte, 1991), Segnosaurus (Perle, 1979), Rinchenia (unpublished photo), Saurornithoides (pers. obs. of AMNH 6516), Zanabazar (Norell et al., 2009), Saurornitholestes (Howse and Milner, 1993), Rahonavis (unpublished photo), Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002), Archaeopteryx (Mayr et al., 2007), Shenzhouraptor (Zhou and Zhang, 2003) and Confuciusornis (Chiappe et al., 1999) lack expanded mid sacrals. Patagonykus (Novas, 1997) does not preserve anterior sacrals, while Mononykus (unpublished photos) does not preserve mid sacrals. Oviraptor (Smith, 1992) does not preserve any sacral vertebrae.

23. This character should be ordered so that strap-like transverse processes are intermediate compared to tapered and expanded processes. Alvarezsaurus (Bonaparte, 1991), Shuvuuia (pers. obs. IGM 100/975), Saurornitholestes (Makovicky, 1995) and Confuciusornis (Chiappe et al., 1999) have distally tapered processes. Troodon (Makovicky, 1995) is polymorphic with both tapered and strap-like processes. Caudipteryx (Zhou and Wang, 2000), Sinornithoides (Paul, 2002), Saurornithoides (pers. obs. AMNH 6516) and Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) have strap-like processes. Gallimimus (Osmolska et al., 1972), Rahonavis (unpublished photo) and Archaeopteryx (Wellnhofer, 1974) are polymorphic, with both strap-like and expanded processes. Allosaurus (Gilmore, 1920), Tyrannosaurus (Brochu, 2003), Garudimimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005), Microraptor (Hwang et al., 2002) and Velociraptor (Norell and Makovicky, 1997) have distally expanded processes. Oviraptor (Smith, 1992) does not preserve any caudal vertebrae. Achillobator (Perle et al., 1999) does not preserve proximal caudals.

24. This character should be ordered so that "slightly longer" is the intermediate state. It is here quantified as "caudal centra 10-15 shorter than caudal centrum 1 (0); 100-200% longer (1); >200% longer (2)". In taxa with incomplete caudal series, it can be estimated based on vertebral elongation. Gorgosaurus (Lambe, 1917), Tyrannosaurus (Brochu, 2003), Chirostenotes (Sues, 1997) and Rinchenia (unpublished photos) have short mid caudals. Articulated Allosaurus tails are rare, but mid caudals are close to the first caudal in length, so it is coded 0/1. Shuvuuia's are coded the same, since mid caudals are close in length to the first complete preserved vertebra, but at least one was present ahead of this (pers. obs. of IGM 100/975). Segnosaurus (Perle, 1979), Microvenator (pers. obs.), Conchoraptor (coding in Maryanska et al., 2002) and Achillobator (Perle et al., 1999) also lack elongate mid caudals. Harpymimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005), Zanabazar (Barsbold, 1974), Adasaurus (unpublished photo) and Utahraptor (Kirkland et al., 1993) have slightly elongate mid caudals. Sinornithoides (Russell and Dong, 1994) is polymorphic with some mid caudals over 200% the first caudal's length. Alvarezsaurus (Bonaparte, 1991) and Troodon (Varricchio et al., 1997) either had slightly or much longer mid caudals. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002), Rahonavis (Forster et al., 1998) and Archaeopteryx (Wellnhofer, 1974) have very elongate mid caudals. Mononykus (Perle et al., 1994) only preserves the first caudal. Oviraptor (Smith, 1992) does not preserve any caudal vertebrae. Confuciusornis (Chiappe et al., 1999) lacks mid caudals, so should be coded inapplicable.

25. This character (Dorsal rib distally narrow (0) or distally wide (1)) is caused by the expanded articulations for sternal ribs. All of the taxa have at least two pairs of expanded ribs when known, and several taxa known from incomplete remains are coded (e.g. Alxasaurus, Troodon, Sinornithosaurus, Achillobator) when their condition is unknown. As this character is correlated to the next (number of sternal ribs) it is here rejected. The only taxon coded differently for each character by Xu and Zhang is Caudipteryx, which they incorrectly coded as having less than four sternal ribs.

26. Pelecanimimus (Senter, pers. comm.), Caudipteryx (Zhou et al., 2000), Saurornitholestes (Codd, 2004), Velociraptor (Codd, 2004) and Archaeopteryx (Wellnhofer, 1974) have more than three pairs of sternal ribs. Alxasaurus (Russell and Dong, 1994), Oviraptor (unpublished photo), "Ingenia" (Psihoyos, 1996), Troodon and Achillobator (Perle et al., 1999) are too incomplete to code.

27. This is here quantified as a furcular arm which is over 36% of scapular length. Tyrannosaurus (Lipkin et al., 2007) has a small furcula. "Ingenia" (unpublished photo) has a large furcula. Sinornithoides cannot be coded as the furcula is proximally incomplete and the scapula is distally incomplete (Currie and Dong, 2001).

28. Alxasaurus (Russell and Dong, 1994), Chirostenotes (Currie and Russell, 1988), "Ingenia" (unpublished photo), Saurornitholestes (Rauhut, 2003) and Utahraptor (unpublished illustration) lack a supracoracoid fenestra. Ornitholestes (Carpenter et al., 2005) does not preserve the pectoral girdle.

29. This character (Localized scapular articular surface for coracoid absent (0) or present (1)) was later elaborated on by Xu et al. (2009) as "Scapula, articular facet for the coracoid, localization absent (0) present, the dorsal portion of the facet extremely thin transversely, but still on the acromion process (1) present, facet limited ventrally, without development on the acromion process (2)." State 1 is coded for maniraptorans, while state 2 is coded for most avialans.
