Xu and Zhang have a coding scheme intermediate between those two distributions, but observation indicates that maniraptorans do not have thinner acromial articulations than other theropods, making Xu et al.'s state 1 problematic. This character is therefore defined as "coracoid articular surface absent on acromion." Avimimus (Kurzanov, 1981), Microraptor (Xu et al., 2003), Saurornitholestes (Rauhut, 2003), Velociraptor (Norell and Makovicky, 1999), Deinonychus (Ostrom, 1974; Brinkman et al., 1998), Scansoriopteryx (Zhang et al., 2002) and Confuciusornis (Chiappe et al., 1999) lack a free acromion. Caudipteryx (pers. obs. of NGMC 97-9-A), Oviraptor (unpublished photo) and Rinchenia (unpublished photo) have a free acromion. Alvarezsaurus (Novas, 1996) is too poorly preserved to code. Ornitholestes (Carpenter et al., 2005) does not preserve the pectoral girdle.

30. Harpymimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005), Caudipteryx (pers. obs. of NGMC 97-9-A), "Ingenia" (unpublished photo), Sinovenator (Xu et al., 2002) and Saurornitholestes (Rauhut, 2003) have subequal scapular and coracoid glenoid contributions. Gorgosaurus (Lambe, 1917), Shuvuuia (Sereno, 2001) and Rinchenia (unpublished photo) have much larger scapular contributions. Alvarezsaurus (Novas, 1996), Oviraptor (unpublished photo) and Rahonavis (unpublished photos) are too poorly preserved to code. Ornitholestes (Carpenter et al., 2005) does not preserve the pectoral girdle.

31. This character (Arm short (0) or very short (1) or long (2) or significantly elongated (3) relative to femur) is problematic in involving multiple independent components (humerus, radius/ulna, metacarpus, digits) and in being correlated with the humeroscapular ratio character 240 (135 in Norell et al., 2001). Using only the humerus and ordering the character, it is revised to be "Humerofemoral ratio <38% (0); 38-69% (1); 70-100% (2); >100% (3)." Patagonykus (Novas, 1997) has either states 0 or 1. Avimimus (Kurzanov, 1981), Microvenator (Makovicky and Sues, 1998), Rinchenia (unpublished photo), Conchoraptor (coding in Maryanska et al., 2002) have humeri 38-69%. Gallimimus (Osmolska et al., 1972), Graciliraptor, Saurornitholestes (femur- Christiensen, 1999; humerus- Jasinoski, 2003 compared to scapula which can be measured in Rauhut, 2003), Deinonychus (Ostrom, 1976) and Unenlagia (Novas et al., 1997) have humeri 70-100%. Struthiomimus (Nicholls and Russell, 1981; Russell, 1972; Osborn, 1916 is polymorphic, with a range of 65-72%. Pelecanimimus (Perez-Moreno et al., 1994), Harpymimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005), Segnosaurus (Perle, 1979), Chirostenotes (Currie and Russell, 1988), Oviraptor (pers. obs.) and Achillobator (Perle et al., 1999) do not preserve all of the necessary elements in single specimens, but those preserved show they should be coded 1/2.

32. Avimimus (Vickers-Rich et al., 2002) lack a crest-like medial tuberosity. Ornitholestes (unpublished photo), Unenlagia (unpublished photo) have a crest-like medial tuberosity. Oviraptor's humerus is too damaged to code (unpublished photo). None of the Caudipteryx (pers. obs. of NGMC 97-9-A; Zhou and Wang, 2000; Zhou et al., 2000) or Archaeopteryx (Wellnhofer, 1974, 1992, 1993; Mayr et al., 2007) specimens have humeri exposed medially to allow one to examine the width of the medial tuber.

33. This is quantified as minimum radius width <72% of ulnar width. Segnosaurus (Perle, 1979), Microvenator (Ostrom, 1978), Rinchenia (unpublished photos) and Troodon (Russell, 1969) have a thick radius. Tyrannosaurus (Brochu, 2003) and Caudipteryx (Zhou et al., 2000) have a thin radius. Archaeopteryx (Wellnhofer, 1974; 1993) is polymorphic. Avimimus (Kurzanov, 1987) does not preserve a radius in described specimens (though Tsuihiji et al., 2009 mention a newly found one).

34. This character should be ordered. As this is a composite of metacarpal I length (character 172 here, or 150 in Norell et al., 2001) and phalanx I-1 length, only the latter is used here. Instead of "Combined lengths of metacarpal I and phalanx I-1 no more than 1.5 times longer (0) or more than 1.9 times longer (1) or shorter (2) than the length of metacarpal II", it is now "Manual phalanx I <70% the length of metacarpal II (0); 70-100% (1); >100% (2)", which agrees most closely with Xu and Zhang's codings. Chirostenotes (Currie, 1990) has a moderate phalanx I-1. Microraptor is polymorphic, as some specimens have moderate phalanx I-1 (Czerkas et al., 2002). Allosaurus (Gilmore, 1920), Gorgosaurus (Lambe, 1917; Matthew and Brown, 1923), Harpymimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005), Shuvuuia (pers. obs. of IGM 100/975; coded inapplicable by Xu and Zhang) and Mononykus (Perle et al., 1994; coded inapplicable by Xu and Zhang) have a long phalanx I-1. Phalanx I-1 of Alxasaurus is only known from proximal and distal ends, making its length uncertain (Russell and Dong, 1994). Manual digit I of Segnosaurus is not preserved (Perle, 1979).

35. This character should be ordered. It is here quantified as "Manual phalanx III-2 >105% of III-1 (0); 60-105% (1); <60% (2)", which best matches Xu and Zhang's codings. Harpymimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005), Gallimimus (Osmolska et al., 1972) and Sinornithoides (Russell and Dong, 1994) have a long phalanx III-2. Struthiomimus (Russell, 1972; Nicholls and Russell, 1981) is polymorphic, with both mid-sized and elongate phalanx III-2. Deinonychus (Ostrom, 1969) has a mid-sized phalanx III-2. "Ingenia" (Barsbold, 1983) has a short phalanx III-2. Caudipteryx (Zhou et al., 2000) cannot be coded as it only has two phalanges on digit III. Ornitholestes (Senter, 2006) does not preserve digit III. Similarly, Alxasaurus (Russell and Dong, 1994) only preserves a partial phalanx from digit III. Shuvuuia (pers. obs. of IGM 100/975) and Mononykus (Perle et al., 1994) should be coded unknown instead of inapplicable since they both had a third digit, though the number of phalanges on it is unknown.

36. Xu and Zhang describe this character as a "prominent proximoventral keel on manual phalanx III-2", and code it as present in dromaeosaurids. Yet Velociraptor (Norell and Makovicky, 1999) and Deinonychus (Ostrom, 1969) lack such a keel. Microraptorians are more difficult to evaluate, but Xu and Wang (2004) state Graciliraptor has a proximoventral HEEL, which could be said to be present in dromaeosaurids. The character is here interpreted as such. Graciliraptor (Xu and Wang, 2004) lack a prominent heel. Allosaurus (Gilmore, 1920), Harpymimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005), Gallimimus (Osmolska et al., 1972), "Ingenia" (Barsbold, 1981) have a heel. Ornitholestes (Senter, 2006) does not preserve digit III. Alxasaurus (Russell and Dong, 1994) only preserves a partial phalanx from digit III. Pelecanimimus (Perez-Moreno et al., 1994) cannot be coded, as it does not expose the ventral side of phalanx III-2. Shuvuuia (pers. obs. of IGM 100/975) and Mononykus (Perle et al., 1994) should be coded unknown instead of inapplicable since they both had a third digit, though the morphology of phalanges on it is unknown.

37. Chirostenotes (Currie and Russell, 1988), Graciliraptor (Xu and Wang, 2004) and Shenzhouraptor (Ji et al., 2002) lack a strong constriction just proximal to the condyles of manual phalanx III-3. Gallimimus (Osmolska et al., 1972) have a strong constriction. Microraptor is polymorphic, as some specimens (e.g. Ji, 2002) lack the constriction. Caudipteryx (Zhou et al., 2000) is inapplicable as it only has two phalanges on digit III. Ornitholestes (Senter, 2006) does not preserve digit III. Alxasaurus (Russell and Dong, 1994) only preserves a partial phalanx from digit III. Pelecanimimus (Perez-Moreno et al., 1994) cannot be coded, as it does not expose the ventral side of phalanx III-3. Shuvuuia (pers. obs. of IGM 100/975) and Mononykus (Perle et al., 1994) should be coded unknown instead of inapplicable since they both had a third digit, though the morphology of phalanges on it is unknown.

38. This is quantified as an ilial length <64% of femoral length. Garudimimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005), Chirostenotes (Currie and Russell, 1988), Conchoraptor (coding in Maryanska et al., 2002), Adasaurus, Deinonychus (Ostrom, 1976), Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) and Shenzhouraptor (Ji et al., 2002) have a long ilium. Velociraptor (Norell and Makovicky, 1999) is polymorphic. Harpymimus' (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005) femur is too incomplete to measure. Mononykus' (Perle et al., 1994) ilium is too incomplete to measure. Oviraptor (pers. obs.) does not preserve a femur or complete ilium.

39. This character is correlated with 177 (Norell et al., 155), so is combined with that character here as the new state "ventral preacetabular hook absent", in which case the character should be ordered. Garudimimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005), Alvarezsaurus (Martinelli and Vera, 2007), Shuvuuia (pers. obs. of IGM 100/975), Chirostenotes (Currie and Russell, 1988), Conchoraptor (coding in Maryanska et al., 2002), Sinovenator (Xu et al., 2002), Saurornitholestes (Hutchinson, 2001), Rahonavis (Forster et al., 1998), Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002), Shenzhouraptor (Ji et al., 2003; Zhang and Zhou, 2003) and Confuciusornis (Chiappe et al., 1999) have a hook. Sinornithoides (Russell and Dong, 1994) lacks a hook. Archaeopteryx is polymorphic as the London specimen has a hook (Novas, 2004). Mononykus (perle et al., 1994) and Oviraptor (pers. obs.) do not preserve the preacetabular process.

40. This is here quantified as an external ilial acetabular rim of <19% ilial length. Garudimimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005), Alvarezsaurus (Bonaparte, 1991), Chirostenotes (Russell and Dong, 1988), Sinovenator (Xu et al., 2002), Troodon (Varricchio et al., 2002), Microraptor (Hwang et al., 2002), Saurornitholestes (Hutchinson, 2001) and Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) have large acetabula. Harpymimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005), Struthiomimus (Osborn, 1916), Shuvuuia (Chiappe et al., 2002), Alxasaurus (Russell and Dong, 1994) and Deinonychus (Ostrom, 1976) have small acetabula. Patagonykus' (Novas, 1997) and Mononykus' (Perle et al., 1994) ilia are too incomplete to measure.

41. Garudimimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005), Alvarezsaurus (Martinelli and Vera, 2007), Patagonykus (Novas, 1997), Chirostenotes (Currie and Russell, 1988), Troodon (Varricchio et al., 2002), Sinornithosaurus (Xu et al., 2002), Saurornitholestes (Hutchinson, 2001) and Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) have vertical or anteriorly projecting pubic peduncles. Alxasaurus (Russell and Dong, 1994), Rinchenia (unpublished photo) and Utahraptor (unpublished illustration) have posteriorly angled pubic peduncles. Oviraptor's peduncle is nearly vertical, but difficult to orient exactly given the poorly preserved ilium (unpublished photo).

42. Harpymimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005), Garudimimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005), Conchoraptor (coding in Makovicky et al., 2005), Saurornitholestes (coding in Makovicky et al., 2005) and Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) lack a midpubic tuber. Patagonykus' pubis (Novas, 1997) is missing a section of midshaft, so cannot be coded. Mononykus' (Perle et al., 1994) only preserves the proximal pubis. Rinchenia (unpublished photos) does not preserve a pubis.

43. Conchoraptor (coding in Makovicky et al., 2005), Troodon (Hutchinson, 2001), Saurornitholestes (Hutchinson, 2001), Velociraptor (Norell and Makovicky, 1999), Utahraptor (unpublished illustration), Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002), Shenzhouraptor (Ji et al., 2002) and Confuciusornis (Chiappe et al., 1999) lack a mid dorsal ischial process. Mononykus (Perle et al., 1994) and Oviraptor (pers. obs.) do not preserve an ischium.

44. Patagonykus (Novas, 1997), Shuvuuia (pers. obs. of IGM 100/1276), Mononykus (Perle et al., 1994), Caudipteryx (Zhou et al., 2000), Avimimus (Vickers-Rich et al., 2002), Byronosaurus (Makovicky et al., 2003), Velociraptor (Norell and Makovicky, 1999), Deinonychus (Ostrom, 1969), Utahraptor (Kirkland et al., 1993), Unenlagia (unpublished photo) and Confuciusornis (Chiappe et al., 1999) lack a groove behind the fibular crest. Allosaurus (Gilmore, 1920), Gallimimus (Osmolska et al., 1972) and Chirostenotes (Currie and Russell, 1988) have a groove behind their fibular crest. Oviraptor (pers. obs.) does not preserve the hindlimb.

45. This character (Pedal digit I proximally located, phalanx I-1 proximal to the distal end of metatarsal III (0) or distally located, phalanx I-1 extending to the level of distal end of metataral III (1)) is correlated with the states of 219 (or Norell et al.'s 203 above) used here. It is therefore ignored.

46. This is best quantified as pedal phalanx II-2 over 82% of the length of II-1. Alvarezsaurus (Bonaparte, 1991), Chirostenotes (Sternberg, 1932), Rinchenia (unpublished photo) and "Ingenia" (Psihoyos, 1996) have pedal phalanx II-2 much shorter than II-2. Saurornitholestes (Longrich and Currie, 2009) has a long phalanx II-2. Ornitholestes (unpublished photos), Garudimimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005), Shuvuuia (pers. obs.) and Segnosaurus (Perle, 1979) do not preserve phalanx II-2. Oviraptor (pers. obs.) does not preserve the hindlimb.

47. This is best quantified as pedal phalanx II-2 distal height >60% of length between centers of articular surfaces. Chirostenotes (Sternberg, 1932), Rinchenia (unpublished photo) and "Ingenia" (Psihoyos, 1996) have a slender pedal phalanx II-2. Gallimimus (Osmoloska et al., 1972), Struthiomimus (Osborn, 1916), Erlikosaurus (Perle, 1981), Avimimus (Kurzanov, 1987), Troodon (Russell, 1969) and Saurornitholestes (Longrich and Currie, 2009) have a stout phalanx II-2. Ornitholestes (unpublished photo), Garudimimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005), Shuvuuia (pers. obs.) and Segnosaurus (Perle, 1979) do not preserve phalanx II-2.

48. Ornitholestes (unpublished photo), Alvarezsaurus (Bonaparte, 1991), Alxasaurus (coding in Makovicky et al., 2005), Segnosaurus (coding in Makovicky et al., 2005), Chirostenotes (coding in Makovicky et al., 2005), Conchoraptor (coding in Makovicky et al., 2005) and Archaeopteryx (Wellnhofer, 1974; Mayr et al., 2007) lack a posterior ridge on metatarsal IV. Sinornithoides (Novas and Pol, 2005), Graciliraptor (Xu and Wang, 2004) and Shenzhouraptor (Agnolin and Novas, 2011) have a ridge. Oviraptor (pers. obs.) does not preserve the hindlimb. The metatarsal IV referred to Dromaeosaurus by Colbert and Russell has been reassigned to Saurornitholestes (Currie, 1995), and has a ridge.

49. Alvarezsaurus (Bonaparte, 1991), Avimimus (Kurzanov, 1987), Sinovenator (White, 2009), Saurornitholestes (unpublished photo), Velociraptor (Norell and Makovicky, 1999) and Deinonychus (Ostrom, 1969) have pedal phalanx IV-4 shorter than IV-3. Shuvuuia (pers. obs. of IGM 100/1276), Chirostenotes (Sternberg, 1932) and Troodon (Russell, 1969) have phalanx IV-4 longer than IV-3. Struthiomimus (Russell, 1972; Nicholls and Russell, 1981) and Sinornithoides (Russell and Dong, 1994) are polymorphic. Harpymimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005), Patagonykus (Novas, 1997), Segnosaurus (Perle, 1979), Pedopenna (Xu and Zhang, 2005) and Rahonavis (Forster et al., 1998) do not preserve phalanx IV-4. Oviraptor (pers. obs.) does not preserve the hindlimb.

50. This is a composite involving metatarsal V length, curvature and mishaft expansion. Only the former is coded for here. It is quantified as metatarsal V over 40% of metatarsal IV length. Segnosaurus (Perle, 1979), Chirostenotes (Sternberg, 1932; Currie and Russell, 1988), Conchoraptor (Barsbold et al., 1990) and Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) have a short metatarsal V. Allosaurus (Madsen, 1976) and Tyrannosaurus (Brochu, 2003) have a long metatarsal V. Ornitholestes (unpublished photos), Shuvuuia (pers. obs.), Mononykus (Perle et al., 1994) and Troodon (Russell, 1969) do not preserve metatarsal V. Oviraptor (pers. obs.) does not preserve the hindlimb.

51. This is a composite involving pedal ungual curvature (0- straight; 1- recurved; 2- strongly recurved), robusticity (0- robust; 2- slender) and cross section (1- thick ventral margin; 2- parallel-sided). Only curvature is coded for here. However, curvature varies between digits (ungual II is ignored here, as it is highly curved in deinonychosaurs, which were not coded as having curved unguals by Xu and Zhang) and Xu and Zhang's codings do not accurately reflect the variation in any digit. Curvature is measured as the depth of the dorsal arc compared to ungual length (measured in a straight line from the proximodorsal tip to the distal tip). Xu and Zhang's codings most closely resemble the curvature of digit I, though there is no difference between taxa coded 1 and 2. The revised character is thus "pedal ungual I curvature <23% (0); >22% (1)." Using this definition, Ornitholestes (unpublished photos; contra Carpenter et al., 2005), Harpymimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005), Patagonykus (Novas, 1997), Shuvuuia (pers. obs.), Alxasaurus (Russell and Dong, 1994) and "Ingenia" (preserved but not described or illustrated well yet) cannot be coded. Microvenator (Makovicky and Sues, 1998), Rinchenia (unpublished photos), Pedopenna (Xu and Zhang, 2005), Sinornithoides (Currie and Dong, 2001), Saurornithoides (pers. obs. of AMNH 6516), Troodon (Russell, 1969) and Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) lack strongly curved hallucial unguals. Deinonychus (Ostrom, 1969) has strongly curved hallucial unguals. Gallimimus (Osmolska et al., 1972), Struthiomimus (Osborn, 1916) and Avimimus (Kurzanov, 1987) are inapplicable as they lack a hallux. Oviraptor (pers. obs.) does not preserve the hindlimb.

52. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) and Shenzhouraptor (Zhou and Zhang, 2002) have round orbits.

53. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) and Shenzhouraptor (coding in Senter, 2003) lack an orbital postorbital process.

54. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) lacks a highly posteriorly convex postorbital bar.

61. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002; Zhang et al., 2002) does not preserve the basisphenoid.

74. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) and Shenzhouraptor (Zhou and Zhang, 2002) have a short dorsal jugal process.

76. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) lacks a jugal recess.

78. Xu and Zhang added a new state to their version of Norell et al.'s character 37 for the T-shaped quadratojugal, now distinguishing between a short and long posterior process. However, the processes in the three eudromaeosaurs coded 2 (Velociraptor, Deinonychus, Dromaeosaurus) are shorter than Erlikosaurus' and equal to some Caudipteryx specimens, both of which were coded 1. The other taxa coded 1 are as short or shorter (e.g. Gallimimus) than the taxa coded 0. Thus the original bistate character is retained. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) has a long process.

80. Both Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) and Shenzhouraptor (Zhou and Zhang, 2002) lack dorsal lacrimal horns at least.

81. Shenzhouraptor (Zhou and Zhang, 2002) has a pneumatic lacrimal.

82. Shenzhouraptor (Zhou and Zhang, 2002) has an elongate posterior lacrimal process and short anterior process.

83. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002; Zhang et al., 2002) does not preserve the skull roof well enough to reject the presence of a prefrontal.

85. Scansoriopteryx (Zhang et al., 2002) lacks a sagittal crest on its parietal.

86. Scansoriopteryx (Zhang et al., 2002) has fused parietals.

87. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) lacks an anteriorly projected ventral squamosal process.

88. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) lacks squamosal-quadratojugal contact.

89. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) lacks a widely separated otic head on its quadrate.

90. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) lacks a strongly inclined quadrate.

91. Xu and Zhang added a new state to this character, for quadrate depressions on the medial surface of the bone, but did not code any taxa as having it. It is therefore left unchanged.

100. Shenzhouraptor (Zhou and Zhang, 2003) has no medial recurvature on its dentary symphysis.

101. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) lacks a large coronoid prominence on its surangular.

102. Shenzhouraptor (Zhou and Zhang, 2002; coded inapplicable by Xu and Zhang, presumably due to the lack of a mandibular fenestra) lacks a posterodorsal dentary process. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) has a process extending over less than half of the fenestra.

103. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) lacks a deep external dentary groove.

104. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) lacks a surangular spine invading its mandibular fenestra.

105. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) has a posterior surangular foramen.

106. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) lacks significant lateral splenial exposure.

108. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) lacks a dorsal articular process. Shenzhouraptor (Zhou and Zhang, 2002) has the process.

109. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) and Shenzhouraptor (Zhou and Zhang, 2002) lack an elongate retroarticular process.

110. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) and Shenzhouraptor (Zhou and Zhang, 2002) lack a caenagnathoid-like jaw joint.

111. Shenzhouraptor (Zhou and Zhang, 2002) lacks premaxillary teeth. The premaxilla of Scansoriopteryx is unpreserved (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002; Zhang et al., 2002).

112. The maxilla of Scansoriopteryx is unpreserved (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002; Zhang et al., 2002).

113. Xu and Zhang add a new state for taxa with some maxillary and dentary teeth unserrated, but this is only true anteriorly in these taxa (all three microraptorians; Sinovenator and Incisivosaurus are both miscoded as they completely lack serrations). As absent premaxillary tooth serrations is completely correlated with it and a separate character added by Senter, this character is left unchanged from Norell et al.'s version. Graciliraptor is thus recoded as lacking mesial serrations. Scansoriopteryx (Zhang et al., 2002) lacks serrations.

114. Graciliraptor (Xu and Wang, 2004) lacks a dentary so cannot be coded for dentary tooth number.

115. Scansoriopteryx (Zhang et al., 2002) lacks serrations, so is inapplicable.

116. Scansoriopteryx (Zhang et al., 2002) lacks serrations, so is inapplicable.

119. Xu and Zhang added a state to distinguish between fused and absent interdental plates, but I agree with Norell et al. that the two states are not distinct.

120. Shenzhouraptor lacks premaxillary teeth (Zhou and Zhang, 2003), so is inapplicable.

121. Shenzhouraptor (Zhou and Zhang, 2002) has less than eleven cervical vertebrae. The condition in Scansoriopteryx is unknown, as it only preserves nine (Zhang et al., 2002).

128. Scansoriopteryx (Zhang et al., 2002) has anteroposteriorly long anterior cervical neural spines.

130. Scansoriopteryx (coding in Zhang et al., 2002) and Shenzhouraptor (coding in Zhou and Zhang, 2002) lack opisthocoelous cervical centra.

132. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) lacks stalked dorsal parapophyses.

133. Shenzhouraptor (coding in Gao et al., 2008) lacks hyposphene-hypantrum articulations.

134. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) lacks posterior dorsal pleurocoels. Shenzhouraptor (Zhou and Zhang, 2003) has them.

138. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) has five sacral vertebrae. Shenzhouraptor (Zhou and Zhang, 2003) has six.

139. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) lacks a ventral keel on its posterior sacral centra.

140. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) lacks sacral pleurocoels.

141. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) and Shenzhouraptor (Zhou and Zhang, 2003) lack a procoelous last sacral.

142. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) has a caudal transition point.

143. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) has less than ten caudals with transverse processes.

145. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) lacks accessory mid caudal neural spines.

146. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) lacks neural spines on distal caudals at least. Graciliraptor (Xu and Wang, 2004) has a dorsal sulcus.

147. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) has mid-sized distal caudal prezygapophyses.

148. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) has between 25 and 40 caudal vertebrae.

149. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) has dorsoventrally compressed proximal chevrons.

151. Scansoriopteryx (Zhang et al., 2002) lacks ossified uncinate processes.

154. Shenzhouraptor (Zhou and Zhang, 2003) has unfused sternal plates.

155. Shenzhouraptor (Zhou and Zhang, 2003) has posterolateral sternal processes.

158. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) and Shenzhouraptor (Jasinoski, 2003) have subglenoid fossae.

159. Shenzhouraptor (Zhou and Zhang, 2002) has an unfused scapulocoracoid.

160. Shenzhouraptor (Zhou and Zhang, 2002) has a deep coracoid.

163. Graciliraptor (Xu and Wang, 2004) has a low-angled deltopectoral crest. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) has a mid-angled crest.

164. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) has a crest on the edge of its deltopectoral crest.

166. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) lacks a strongly convex distal ulna.

168. The supposed centrale in Graciliraptor (Xu and Wang, 2004) may be an ulnare in extensor view, as the rest of the manus is in this view and it matches the shape of Allosaurus' ulnare. Thus it cannot be coded for ulnare shape in proximal view.

169. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) has fused distal carpals I and II.

171. Shenzhouraptor (Ji et al., 2003) has a large semilunate carpal. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) has a small semilunate carpal.

174. Shenzhouraptor is here conservatively coded 0/1 for manual ungual I curvature, given my more restrictive and quantified definiton of character states and the small available photos (Zhou and Zhang, 2002; Ji et al., 2003).

176. As this character is here redefined to only code for a proximodorsal lip on manual ungual I, Graciliraptor (Xu and Wang, 2004) is recoded as lacking one. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) has a lip.

177. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) has a small ventral hook on its preacetabular process.

178. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) lacks a pointed postacetabular process.

180. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) lacks a deep brevis fossa.

182. Shenzhouraptor is coded inapplicable by Xu and Zhang, but does have a cuppedicus fossa (Zhou and Zhang, 2003), though information is still unavailable regarding its extent over the pubic peduncle. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) has an anteriorly restricted cuppedicus fossa.

183. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) lacks a cuppedicus fossa. Shenzhouraptor (Zhou and Zhang, 2003) has a laterally overhanging cuppedicus fossa.

184. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) lacks a proximodorsal ischial process.

185. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) lacks a ventrally curved distal ischium.

186. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) and Shenzhouraptor (Ji et al., 2003) lack an obturator process.

187. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) and Shenzhouraptor (Ji et al., 2003) should be coded inapplicable, since they lack an obturator process.

188. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) lacks an obturator notch or foramen.

190. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) has a long ischium.

192. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) has an ischial boot. Shenzhouraptor (Ji et al., 2003) lacks an ischial boot.

193. Shenzhouraptor (Zhou and Zhang, 2002) has a mesopubic pelvis. Notably, Xu and Zhang correctly coded Scansoriopteryx, though the specimen they used lacks pelvic material.

194. Xu and Zhang divided a state in this character to distinguish between the supposedly hooked posterior pubic boots of Adasaurus, Velociraptor, Unenlagia, Archaeopteryx and Shenzhouraptor, and the unhooked boots of Sinornithoides, Sinovenator and microraptorians. Yet of these, only Unenlagia and some Archaeopteryx (e.g. Eischatt) have the character. In addition, many taxa such as Allosaurus and ornithomimosaurs would be considered to have a hooked pubic boot if their pubes were more opisthopubic. As pubic boot orientation is unrelated to pubic boot size, Xu and Zhang's states are not incorporated here. Thus Shenzhouraptor is coded as having only a posterior boot (Zhou and Zhang, 2002), while Scansoriopteryx lacks any significant boot (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002).

196. Xu and Zhang are like Calvo et al. in adding a state for posterior pubic curvature, but do not actually code any taxa as possessing this. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) has a straight pubis.

198. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) has a widely separated anterior trochanter.

200. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) lacks a posterior trochanter. Shenzhouraptor (coding in Zhou and Zhang, 2002) has a posterior trochanter.

201. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) lacks a fourth trochanter.

202. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) lacks an accessory trochanter.

203. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) lacks a medial epicondyle on its femur.

204. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) and Shenzhouraptor (coding in Zhou and Zhang, 2002) lack an enclosed popliteal fossa.

205. Shenzhouraptor (coding in Zhou and Zhang, 2002) lacks fibular-tarsal contact.

208. Pedopenna (Xu and Zhang, 2005) and Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) have shallow tibiotarsal condyles.

209. Shenzhouraptor (coding in Zhou and Zhang, 2002) lacks a medial cnemial crest.

210. Xu and Zhang add a state distinguishing tall and narrow astragalar ascending processes from tall and broad processes. Yet all four taxa coded as having tall and narrow processes (Segnosaurus, Pedopenna, Sinornithosaurus and Archaeopteryx) actually have a broad process covering most of the anterior tibial surface. Their new state is thus not incorporated here, and would make the character a composite in any case. Thus both Pedopenna and Graciliraptor are recoded as simply having a tall process, which is also true for Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) and Shenzhouraptor (Zhou and Zhang, 2002).

211. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) and Shenzhouraptor (Zhou and Zhang, 2002) have a groove across the base of their astragalar ascending process.

212. Shenzhouraptor (Zhou and Zhang, 2002) has a tibia unfused to its tarsus. Pedopenna (Xu and Zhang, 2005) has at least partial fusion.

214. Pedopenna (Xu and Zhang, 2005) and Graciliraptor (Xu and Wang, 2004) lack at least distal metatarsal fusion.

215. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) and Shenzhouraptor (Zhou and Zhang, 2006) lack a deeply ginglymoid metatarsal II.

216. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) lacks a deeply ginglymoid metatarsal III.

217. Xu and Zhang add a state for subarctomatarsaly to the ordered range of metatarsal morphologies. Unfortunately, subarctometatarsaly is somewhat difficult to define. Xu and Zhang and Novas and Pol (2005) distinguish it from the plesiomorphic condition by a proximal transverse pinching and a distally triangular section. Makovicky et al. (2005) only use the proximal pinching, which seems like a better idea as it does not create a composite character. Harpymimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005), Garudimimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005), Caudipteryx (Zhou and Wang, 2000), Velociraptor (Norell and Makovicky, 1999), Deinonychus (Ostrom, 1969) and Archaeopteryx (Mayr et al., 2007) have a subarctometatarsus. Conchoraptor (Barsbold et al., 1990) has a proximally incomplete metatarsal III that may be either subarctometatarsal or not. Whether the third metatarsal is anteriorly exposed at the proximal end is uncertain in Pedopenna (Xu and Zhang, 2005) and Sinornithoides (Currie and Dong, 2001), so they are coded as having either a subarctometatarsus or an arctometatarsus. Saurornithoides (Norell et al., 2009) and Graciliraptor (Xu and Wang, 2004) have a constricted third metatarsal, but their condition cannot be determined past that.

219. Pedopenna (Xu and Zhang, 2005) has a distally placed hallux.

222. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) lacks a lateral squamosal shelf.

223. Shenzhouraptor (Zhou and Zhang, 2002) lacks a large lateral quadrate tab.

224. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) and Shenzhouraptor (Zhou and Zhang, 2002) lack a sharply angled postorbital process on the frontal.

225. Shenzhouraptor should be coded inapplicable as it lacks premaxillary teeth (Zhou and Zhang, 2003).

226. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) has a notch in its anterior frontal.

229. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) has a triangular dentary. Shenzhouraptor (Zhou and Zhang, 2002) has a non-triangular dentary.

230. Shenzhouraptor (Zhou and Zhang, 2002) has an anteriorly convex prearticular.

231. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) and Shenzhouraptor (Zhou and Zhang, 2003) lack a fused zygapophyseal ridge on their sacrum.

232. Shenzhouraptor (Zhou and Zhang, 2003; Ji et al., 2003) has a naris which overlaps its antorbital fossa.

241. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) has an elongate preacetabular process.

244. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) has a strongly rounded anterior preacetabular edge.

245. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) lacks a prominent supracetabular crest at least.

248. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002; Zhang et al., 2002) lacks a lateral dentary shelf.

251. Graciliraptor (Xu and Wang, 2004) has anteriorly bifurcated chevrons.

252. Shenzhouraptor (coding in Zhou and Zhang, 2002) lacks an obturator tuber. Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) has an obturator tuber.

256. Sinosauropteryx (Currie and Chen, 2001) and Shenzhouraptor (Zhou and Zhang, 2003; Ji et al., 2003) lack metatarsal remiges.

257. No taxon is coded as lacking this character by Xu and Zhang, making it uninformative. Sinornithosaurus (Xu et al., 2001), Velociraptor (Turner et al., 2007) and Scansoriopteryx (Czerkas and Yuan, 2002) have pennaceous feathers.

258. Xu and Zhang list this character (robust proximal metatarsal IV, equivalent to Xu et al.'s (2002) character 206), but do not code any taxa for it.

259. Xu and Zhang also list this character without coding it. It's listed as metatarsals II-IV subequal in length, and is stated in the text to be present in Pedopenna, Microraptor and Scansoriopteryx. As the length of metatarsals II and IV vary independently compared to III, and several other taxa have an elongate metatarsal IV (e.g. Shuvuuia, Segnosaurus, Sinornithoides, Rahonavis), the character is here refined as metatarsal II over 97% the length of metatarsal III. Notably, Microraptor is polymorphic, as neither the specimens described by Hwang et al. (2002) or NGMC 00-12-A (Ji, 2002) have a metatarsal II more elongate than many other taxa (Harpymimus, some Gallimimus, Shuvuuia, Avimimus, Sinornithosaurus, Rahonavis, some Archaeopteryx).

 

Novas and Pol (2005) on Neuquenraptor

Novas and Pol added Neuquenraptor to Xu and Norell's (2004) matrix

186. The distal femur is missing in Neuquenraptor (Novas and Pol, 2005), so that the presence of an anteromedial crest is uncertain.

188. Neuquenraptor (Novas and Pol, 2005) has fibular-tarsal contact based on the groove in the tibia.

193. Neuquenraptor (Novas and Pol, 2005) has a tall astragalar ascending process.

197. Neuquenraptor (Novas and Pol, 2005) does not preserve the proximal metatarsus, so only distal fusion can be excluded.

200. Novas and Pol added a state for the subarctometatarsus, as in Xu and Zhang (2005).

202. Neuquenraptor (Novas and Pol, 2005) does not have an articulated hallux, so its position is uncertain.

215. Neuquenraptor (Novas and Pol, 2005) lacks a lateral femoral ridge.

223. Novas and Pol added this character for the posterior flange on metatarsal IV of basal deinonychosaurs, but I follow Makovicky et al. (2005) in coding this as homologous to the medial flange in derived dromaeosaurids and derived troodontids. This is the same as Xu and Zhang's (2005) character 48. Mononykus (Perle et al., 1994) cannot be coded, as most of metatarsal IV's shaft is unpreserved.

 

Makovicky et al. (2005) on Buitreraptor

20. Buitreraptor (Makovicky et al., 2005) has an elongate subnarial premaxilla process that extends posterior to the naris.

22. Buitreraptor (Gianechini et al., 2011) does not preserve the premaxilla, so the presence of a crenulated ventral edge is unknown.

31. Buitreraptor (Makovicky et al., 2005) has a short dorsal jugal process.

32. Buitreraptor (Makovicky et al., 2005) lacks a rod-like posterior jugal process.

42. Buitreraptor (Agnolin and Novas, 2011) lacks a sinusoidal supratemporal fossa margin.

44. Buitreraptor (Makovicky et al., 2005) does not preserve the anterior articular surface of the frontal, so cannot be coded for the presence of a notch.

45. Buitreraptor (Agnolin and Novas, 2011) has a parietal sagittal crest.

46. Buitreraptor (Agnolin and Novas, 2011) has unfused parietals.

47. Buitreraptor (Gianechini and Apesteguia, 2011) does not preserve the ventral squamosal process, so its angle is unknown.

51. Buitreraptor (Makovicky et al., 2005) has a strongly inclined quadrate.

65. Buitreraptor (Makovicky et al., 2005) does not preserve the dentary symphysis, so cannot be coded for recurvature.

70. Buitreraptor (Makovicky et al., 2005) has a non-triangular dentary.

75. Buitreraptor (Makovicky et al., 2005) lacks significant lateral splenial exposure.

82. Buitreraptor (Makovicky et al., 2005) has maxillary teeth.

84. Makovicky et al. eliminated the third state (more than thirty dentary teeth), though as noted under the Norell et al. 2001 discussion (character 86), most of the derived taxa have this state instead of the second one (25-30 teeth).

85. Though not indicated as such, this character coding for dentary teeth being placed in a common groove is new to the TWG matrices. IGM 100/44 (Barsbold et al., 1987) has dentary alveoli. Incisivosaurus (Balanoff et al., 2009) has some dentary teeth placed in a groove. Garudimimus, Gallimimus, Struthiomimus, Dromiceiomimus, Caudipteryx, Avimimus, Chirostenotes, Microvenator, Oviraptor, Rinchenia, IGM 100/42, Conchoraptor, "Ingenia" and Confuciusornis should all be coded inapplicable as they lack dentary teeth. Shenzhousaurus does not preserve any interdental septa or lingual wall (Ji et al., 2003), so cannot be coded. Achillobator (Perle et al., 1999), Utahraptor (Kirkland et al., 1993; Britt et al., 2001) and Rahonavis (Forster et al., 1998) do not preserve dentaries, so cannot be coded. Note that in some taxa like Incisivosaurus and Troodon, this only affects a certain portion of the tooth row. Furthermore, Makovicky et al.'s codings suggest a rather indiscriminate coding method where any taxon preserving cranial material which isn't supposed to have a groove is coded that way, while all troodontids were coded as having grooves. Thus taxa with poorly preserved/described dentaries such as Saurornithoides and Adasaurus may have been coded without justification.

90. Buitreraptor (Agnolin and Novas, 2011) does not preserve the lingual alveolar margin, so cannot be coded for interdental plates.

99. Buitreraptor (unpublished photo) has a long neural spine on cervical five at least.

107. Due to the redefinition of this character (anterior dorsal transverse processes short), Buitreraptor is conservatively coded unknown until dorsal views of its anterior dorsals are examined.

116. Makovicky et al. add an extra state for taxa with less than seven caudals with transverse processes, coding Archaeopteryx and Confuciusornis this way. The character should be ordered. Microraptor (Hwang et al., 2002) has less than seven with transverse processes. Archaeopteryx is polymorphic, as some specimens (Eichstatt- Wellnhofer, 1974) have more than seven caudals with transverse processes. Confuciusornis (Chiappe et al., 1999; Goernemann, 1999) has seven free caudals, all with transverse processes. Thus it is here coded 0/1, since the pygostyle contains vertebrae which cannot be coded.

120. Buitreraptor (Makovicky et al., 2005) has moderately elongated distal caudal prezygapophyses.

159. Buitreraptor (unpublished photo) has divergent postacetabular processes.

166. Makovicky et al. add this character- Ischium with rodlike shaft [i.e. part distal to acetabular portion](0) or with wide, flat, and plate-like shaft (1). It is coded as present in therizinosaurs, oviraptorosaurs and paravians. Yet the ischial shaft proximal to the obturator process is similarly compressed in Allosaurus (41% of depth- Gilmore, 1920) and Saurornithoides (47%- pers. obs.). Assuming a similar transverse width in theropod ischia, those of maniraptorans are deeper for more of their length primarily due to their distally placed obturator processes. Not only is there more deep area proximal to the obturator process, but the generally similar amount of distal taper leaves less of the ischium to be rod-like. Indeed, the only taxa coded by Makovicky et al. as having plate-like ischia which also have proximally placed obturator processes are Archaeornithomimus (described by Smith and Galton 1990 as having a rounded distal shaft, so probably miscoded) and Achillobator (which is described as compressed by Perle et al. 1999, and does retain its depth distally). Until an exact area of the ischium is specified as being more compressed in maniraptorans, and this is found to be independent of obturator placement, the character is rejected.

167. Though Makovicky et al. wisely redefine this character to only involve dorsoventral curvature (Ischiadic shaft straight (0) or ventrodistally curved anteriorly (1) or hooked posteriorly (2)), they do not actually change the codings from Norell et al.'s original character which also had states for obturator process medial flexure and ischial lateral concavity. The new state is added here and the character ordered, which also necessitates making a straight tip the middle state. Here Gorgosaurus, Chirostenotes, Troodon, Sinornithosaurus, Saurornitholestes, Adasaurus, Velociraptor, Deinonychus, Achillobator, Buitreraptor and Archaeopteryx are coded as having dorsally curved distal ischia, while Allosaurus, Sinosauropteryx, Compsognathus, Shenzhousaurus, Anserimimus, Alxasaurus, Segnosaurus, Caudipteryx, "Ingenia", Sinornithoides, Saurornithoides and Confuciusornis have distally straight ischia. Microraptor is polymorphic, with some specimens having dorsally curved tips, and others being straight.

168. Makovicky et al. add a character describing the convexity of the lateral ischial surface - Lateral face of ischiadic blade flat [or round in rodlike ischia] (0) or laterally concave (1) or with longitudinal ridge subdividing lateral surface into anterior (including obturator process) and posterior parts (2). Their description indicates that state 2 can involve a subtle ridge which "forms a slight medial flexure of the obturator process", meaning this incorporates parts of the old version of 167. State 1 is also from the old 167, but oddly Makovicky only use two states in their matrix, with those taxa coded as state 1 obviously meant to be those exhibiting state 2. This character is here ordered and changed so that laterally concave shafts are state 0 while flat or rounded shafts are state 1. Compsognathus (photo of cast), Patagonykus (Novas, 1997), Caudipteryx (Zhou et al., 2000), Conchoraptor (Lu, 2004), Microraptor (Xu et al., 2000), Saurornitholestes (Hutchinson, 2001) and Achillobator (Perle et al., 1999) have a laterally concave ischium. Deinonychus (Ostrom, 1969) has the same condition as carnosaurs- the ischial shaft is laterally convex except for a flexure at the obturator process base. Contra Makovicky et al., I do not find the convexity dorsal to this flexure homologous with the lateral ridge in Buitreraptor, as the latter ridge extends proximally along the middle of the shaft instead of ending with the obturator process itself at the ventral ischial margin. Velociraptor (Norell and Makovicky, 1997) is similar, except that the ischial body above the obturator process is concave, so it is here coded 0. Archaeopteryx is polymorphic, as the London specimen (Witmer lab photo) is convex except for slight obturator flexure, while the Eichstatt specimen (Wellnhofer, 1974) has a concave distal shaft. Similarly, in Gorgosaurus (Lambe, 1917) the left ischium is strongly concave down the center, while the right only has a concavity at the distal end of the obturator process. Archaeornithomimus (pers. obs. of AMNH 6558) lacks a ridge, but may be either slightly concave or flat. Shuvuuia (pers. obs. of IGM 100/975), Segnosaurus (Zanno, 2010), Sinovenator (Xu et al., 2002), Rahonavis (unpublished photos) and Confuciusornis (Chiappe et al., 1999) have a convex ischium. Harpymimus' ischium (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005) is too incomplete to code. Garudimimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005) and Oviraptor (pers. obs.) do not preserve an ischium.

169. Buitreraptor (Makovicky et al., 2005) has an obturator process placed at midlength.

171. Buitreraptor (Makovicky et al., 2005) has an obturator notch.

175. Buitreraptor (Makovicky et al., 2005) lacks an ischial boot.

180. Makovicky et al. add the state for a posteriorly curved pubic shaft, as Calvo et al. (2004) and Xu and Zhang (2005) did. Velociraptor (Norell and Makovicky, 1997), Deinonychus (Ostrom, 1976), Rahonavis (unpublished photos) and Archaeopteryx (Mayr et al., 2007) are miscoded as having posteriorly curved pubes. Microraptor (Xu et al., 2003) is miscoded as having a straight pubis. Sinovenator (Xu et al., 2002; unpublished photo) is polymorphic.

182. This character should be ordered. Gorgosaurus (Lambe, 1917), Caudipteryx (Hutchinson, 2001), Deinonychus (Ostrom, 1976), Rahonavis (unpublished photo) and Confuciusornis (Chiappe et al., 1999) lack an interpubic slit. Segnosaurus (unpublished photo of IGM 100/80) has an interpubic slit or no apron contact. Patagonykus (Novas, 1997) and Shuvuuia (Chiappe et al., 2002) lack pubic apron contact. Shenzhousaurus (Ji et al., 2003), Harpymimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005) and Saurornithoides (Norell and Makovicky, 1999) have pubic apron contact at least.

184. Buitreraptor (unpublished photo) lacks a fused trochanteric crest.

187. Buitreraptor (unpublished photo) has almost no trace of a fourth trochanter, so is here coded as lacking one.

189. Buitreraptor (Makovicky et al., 2005) lacks a medial epicondyle on the femur.

194. Buitreraptor (unpublished photo) has a shallow tibiotarsal intercondylar sulcus.

200. Buitreraptor (Makovicky et al., 2005) can only be coded as definitely lacking distal metatarsal fusion, as the proximal metatarsus is unpreserved.

201. Buitreraptor (Gianechini and Apesteguia, 2011) has only a "partially developed" ginglymoid articulation on metatarsal II.

202. Buitreraptor (Gianechini and Apesteguia, 2011) has only a very slightly ginglymoid articulation on metatarsal III.

203. Makovicky et al. add a state for subarctometatarsal metatarsi, like Xu and Zhang (2005) and Novas and Pol (2005). Buitreraptor (Gianechini and Apesteguia, 2011) can only be coded as subarctometatarsal or arctometatarsal, as the proximal metatarsus is unpreserved.

209. Buitreraptor (unpublished photos) has distally expanded dorsal neural spines.

211. Buitreraptor (Makovicky et al., 2005) seems to have fused the surangular and angular, so is coded inapplicable for posterior angular extent.

217. Buitreraptor (Agnolin and Novas, 2011) has a laterally visible brevis fossa.

218. Buitreraptor (Makovicky et al., 2005) has a lateral femoral ridge.

219. Buitreraptor (Agnolin and Novas, 2011) lacks supratemporal fossa excavation on its squamosal.

220. Buitreraptor (Makovicky et al., 2005) has a fully toothed dentary.

223. Buitreraptor (unpublished photo) lacks a supraglenoid buttress.

226. Rinchenia (unpublished photo), Sinornithoides (Russell and Dong, 1994), Troodon (Varricchio et al., 2002) lack a dorsally concave postacetabular process. Gorgosaurus (Lambe, 1917), Tyrannosaurus (Brochu, 2003), Harpymimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005), Gallimimus (Osmolska et al., 1972), Struthiomimus (Osborn, 1916), Dromiceiomimus (Parks, 1933), Anserimimus (unpublished photo), Alvarezsaurus (Martinelli and Vera, 2007), Segnosaurus (Zanno, 2010), Avimimus (Kurzanov, 1987), Chirostenotes (Currie and Russell, 1988), Oviraptor (Smith, 1992), IGM 100/42 (unpublished photo), "Ingenia" (Psihoyos, 1996), Sinovenator (Xu et al., 2002), Sinornithosaurus (unpublished photo), Adasaurus (Barsbold, 1983), Saurornitholestes (Hutchinson, 2001), Achillobator (Perle et al., 1999) have a dorsally concave postacetabular process. Caudipteryx is polymorphic, as seen in the right and left ilia of IVPP V12430 (Zhou et al., 2000). Archaeopteryx is polymorphic, as the Munich specimen (Wellnhofer, 1993) has a concave process. Pelecanimimus (Perez-Moreno et al., 1994), Shenzhousaurus (Ji et al., 2003), Garudimimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005), Archaeornithomimus (Hutchinson, 2001), Shuvuuia (pers. obs. of IGM 100/975), Mononykus (Perle et al., 1994), Microvenator (Makovicky and Sues, 1998) cannot be coded, as the dorsal postacetabular margin is too poorly preserved.

227. Archaeornithomimus (Smith and Galton, 1990) and Rinchenia (unpublished photo) lack a lobate postacetabular process. While Makovicky et al. state "The reduced brevis shelf of Unenlagia also appears to be slightly lobate", the almost symmetrically expanded postacetabular process is similar in shape to many plesiomorphic taxa (e.g. compare to Tyrannosaurus in Novas, 2004 fig. 7.3), so it is coded as absent here. Shuvuuia (pers. obs. of IGM 100/975), Velociraptor (Norell and Makovicky, 1997) have a lobate process. Microraptor is polymorphic, as the holotype (Xu et al., 2000) does not have a lobate process. Compsognathus' holotype does not preserve the postacetabular process (Ostrom, 1978), while the referred specimen only preserves a sagittal section of the area (Peyer, 2006), so it cannot be coded. Mononykus (Perle et al., 1994), Incisivosaurus (Xu et al., 2002) and Microvenator (Makovicky and Sues, 1998) cannot be coded, as the posterior ilium is unpreserved.

228. While Makovicky et al. define the derived state not only by the size of the proximoventral heel on pedal phalanx II-2, but also by its supposed confinement to the medial side of the proximal intercotylar ridge, supposedly basal taxa like Buitreraptor (unpublished photo), Unenlagia paynemili (Porfiri et al., 2011) and Hesperonychus (Longrich and Currie, 2009) show the lateral cotyla extending onto the heel when seen in lateral view, which is also confirmed by Senter (2010) for Sinornithoides. Thus only the size is used here, and taxa without a heel are coded with a new state 0. Taxa with a small heel are then coded state 1, and those with a large heel coded state 2, and the character is ordered. A large heel is defined as one >43% of the distal articulation height. Taxa without a heel are- Sinraptor (Currie and Zhao, 1994), Allosaurus (Madsen, 1976), Gorgosaurus (Lambe, 1917), Tyrannosaurus (Brochu, 2003), Huaxiagnathus (Hwang et al., 2004), Sinosauropteryx (unpublished photo of NIGP 127587), Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006), Harpymimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005), Archaeornithomimus (pers. obs. of AMNH 6570), Gallimimus (Osmolska et al., 1972), Struthiomimus (Osborn, 1916), Dromiceiomimus (Parks, 1933), Anserimimus (Bronowicz, 2011), Alvarezsaurus (Bonaparte, 1991), Mononykus (unpublished photo), Alxasaurus (Russell and Dong, 1994), Erlikosaurus (Perle, 1981), Caudipteryx (pers. obs. of NGMC 97-9-A), Avimimus (Kurzanov, 1987), Rinchenia (unpublished photo), "Ingenia" (Psihoyos, 1996), Archaeopteryx (Wellnhofer, 1974) and Confuciusornis (Chiappe et al., 1999). IGM 100/44 (Barsbold et al., 1987), Sinornithoides (Currie and Dong, 2001), Byronosaurus (Makovicky et al., 2005), Troodon (Russell, 1969) and Microraptor (Hwang et al., 2002) have a large heel. Saurornithoides' (pers. obs.) and Dromaeosaurus' (unpublished photos) are of uncertain length, so are coded 1/2.

229. This character coding for a posterior metatarsal IV ridge was added by Xu and Zhang (2005) as 48 and Novas and Pol (2005) as 223.

230. This new character of Makovicky et al. (large proximodorsal ischial process) is here added as an extra ordered state to Norell et al.'s character 166 coding for the presence of the process. While Archaeopteryx is correctly said to be polymorphic in the character description, Makovicky et al. only code it as having a small process.

231. This is the same character (pubic tubercle located distally on shaft) that was added by Xu and Zhang (2005) as character 42. Archaeopteryx (Petronievics and Woodward, 1917) lacks a midpubic tubercle. Huaxiagnathus (Hwang et al., 2004) has the pubic shaft blocked by the femur. In both Compsognathus specimens (Ostrom, 1978; Peyer, 2006), the pubic shaft is only preserved as a medial impression. Alxasaurus (Russell and Dong, 1994) does not preserve the pubis.

232. This is the same character (mid dorsal ischial process) that was added by Xu and Zhang (2005) as character 43. Unenlagia comahuensis (Gianechini and Apesteguia, 2011), Utahraptor (unpublished illustration) and Confuciusornis (Goernemann, 1999) lack a mid dorsal ischial process. Segnosaurus (Zanno, 2010), Mei (Xu and Norell, 2004) and Sinovenator (Xu et al., 2002) have a process. Pelecanimimus (Perez-Moreno et al., 1994), Patagonykus (Novas, 1997) cannot be coded.

233. Segnosaurus (Zanno, 2010) and Archaeopteryx (Wellnhofer, 1974, 1993; Mayr et al., 2007) have a postobturator notch. Allosaurus (Chure, 2000) and Microraptor (notch present in CAGS 20-8-001; Hwang et al., 2002) are polymorphic. Sinosauropteryx (unpublished photo of NIGP 127587), Alxasaurus (Russell and Dong, 1994), Troodon (Hutchinson, 2001), Utahraptor (unpublished illustration) lack a postobturator notch. While Ornitholestes' right ischium appears to have a postobturator notch (unpublished photos), the left ischium shows this is a break. Shuvuuia (pers. obs. of IGM 100/975) and Confuciusornis (Goernemann, 1999) should be coded inapplicable, as they lack an obturator process. Patagonykus (Novas, 1997), Avimimus (Kurzanov, 1987) and Unenlagia (Gianechini and Apesteguia, 2011) do not preserve the distal obturator area.

234. While defined by Makovicky et al. as "Triangular obturator process with short rostral projection and wide base along ischial shaft (0) or with short base, long process extending rostrally (1)", there is no reason to exclude taxa with quadrangular processes, since the rostral projection is homologous to the proximal projecting corner. Thus Sinraptor (Currie and Zhao, 1994) and Allosaurus (Gilmore, 1920) lack a narrow process. The character is here quentified as "angle between proximal and distal edges of obturator process <30 degrees". Sinosauropteryx (Currie and Chen, 2001), Segnosaurus (Zanno, 2010), Troodon (Hutchinson, 2001), Sinovenator (Xu et al., 2002), Unenlagia comahuensis (Gianechini and Apesteguia, 2011), Utahraptor (unpublished illustration) have a stout process. Archaeopteryx (Petronievics and Woodward, 1917; Wellnhofer, 1974, 1993; Mayr et al., 2007) is polymorphic. Shenzhousaurus (Ji et al., 2003), Shuvuuia (pers. obs. of IGM 100/975) and Confuciusornis (Goernemann, 1999) should be coded inapplicable, as they lack an obturator process. Garudimimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005), Patagonykus (Novas, 1997), Avimimus (Kurzanov, 1987), Microvenator (Makovicky and Sues, 1998) and Zanabazar (Norell et al., 2009) do not preserve the obturator process.

235. Huaxiagnathus (Hwang et al., 2004), Sinosauropteryx (unpublished photo of NIGP 127587), Ornitholestes (unpublished photo), Erlikosaurus (Barsbold and Perle, 1980) lack a dorsal tubercle on metatarsal II. Allosaurus (Madsen, 1976), Velociraptor (Norell and Makovicky, 1997) have a dorsal tubercle on metatarsal II. Tyrannosaurus is polymorphic, as FMNH PR2081 (Brochu, 2003) has a short ridge in this area. Mononykus (Perle et al., 1994) and IGM 100/44 (Barsbold et al., 1987) cannot be coded, as most of the shaft of metatarsal II is unpreserved. Sinornithosaurus (Xu and Wang, 2000) cannot be coded as its second metatarsal is only exposed ventrally. Achillobator (Perle et al., 1999) does not preserve metatarsal II.

236. This character (coding for ulnohumeral ratios) is correlated with Xu and Zhang's (2005) character 31 coding for arm length, which was redefined here to only measure humeral length. It is thus rejected.

 

Kirkland et al. (2005) on Falcarius

2. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2009) has a round orbit.

3. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2009) lacks an orbital process on the postorbital.

4. Falcarius (Zanno, 2010) and Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2009) lack an upcurved anterior postorbital process.

5. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2009) lacks a posteriorly convex postorbital bar.

6. Nothronychus (Smith et al., 2011) lacks confluent subotic and anterior tympanic recesses.

7. Nothronychus (Smith et al., 2011) does not preserve the crista interfenestralis, so cannot be coded for how recessed it is.

8. Falcarius (Smith et al., 2011) and Nothronychus (Smith et al., 2011) have a subotic recess, which was probably miscoded due to Hwang et al. switching their states.

9. The position of the basisphenoid recess cannot be determined in Falcarius due to fusion (Smith et al., 2011). Nothronychus (Kirkland et al., 2005) lacks a recess.

10. Nothronychus should be coded inapplicable for divisions within its basisphenoid recess, since it lacks the structure (Kirkland et al., 2005).

12. Falcarius (Smith et al., 2011) lacks laterally projected basipterygoid processes. Nothronychus should be coded inapplicable for the angle of its basipterygoid processes, since it lacks the structures (Kirkland et al., 2005).

13. Falcarius (Smith et al., 2011) and Nothronychus (Kirkland et al., 2005) have poorly developed basipterygoid processes.

14. Nothronychus should be coded inapplicable for the pneumaticity of its basipterygoid processes, since it lacks the structures (Kirkland et al., 2005).

15. Falcarius (Smith et al., 2011) has basipterygoid recesses. Nothronychus should be coded inapplicable for recesses on its basipterygoid processes, since it lacks the structures (Kirkland et al., 2005).

16. Falcarius (Smith et al., 2011) is polymorphic in that one specimen has a shallow dorsal tympanic recess, but another lacks it.

17. Falcarius (Smith et al., 2011) lacks an accessory recess dorsal to the interfenestral crest.

18. Falcarius (Smith et al., 2011) has a posterior tympanic recess on its paroccipital process.

20. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2009) has maxillary-naris contact.

25. Falcarius (Zanno, 2010) and Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2009) have an extensive maxillary palatal shelf.

26. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2009) lacks a ventral palatal process.

31. Falcarius (Zanno, 2010) and Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2009) lack a highly pneumatized nasal.

32. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2009) has a short dorsal jugal process.

36. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2009) has a short posterior quadratojugal process.

38. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2009) lacks a dorsal lacrimal horn.

40. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2009) has short anterior and posterior lacrimal processes.

41. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2009) has a large prefrontal.

42. Falcarius (Zanno, 2010) has an obtuse nasofrontal suture.

52. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2009) seems to lack a posteriorly inclined quadrate.

54. Falcarius (Zanno, 2010) has a wide lateral quadrate tab.

66. Falcarius (Zanno, 2010) has a strongly medially curved dentary symphysis.

68. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2009) lacks a strong surangular coronoid process.

69. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2009) lacks a posterodorsal dentary process that extends over most of the mandibular fenestra at least.

71. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2009) has a triangular dentary.

72. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2009) lacks a deep lateral dentary groove.

73. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2009) lacks a surangular spine piercing the mandibular fenestra.

74. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2009) has a slit-like internal mandibular fenestra.

75. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2009) has a posterior surangular foramen.

76. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2009) has a splenial with narrow lateral exposure.

80. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2009) has a non-caenagnathoid-like jaw articulation.

81. Falcarius (Zanno, 2010) and Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2009) have premaxillary teeth.

83. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2009) has maxillary teeth. The teeth of Nothronychus are isolated and the illustrated crown's height resembles an anterior dentary tooth of Erlikosaurus (Kirkland and Wolfe, 2001), so it is here coded unknown for the presence of maxillary teeth.

85. Nothronychus (Kirkland and Wolfe, 2001) does not preserve a dentary, so cannot be coded for dentary tooth number.

86. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 1999) has large serrations.

89. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 1999) has evenly spaced dentary teeth.

90. Falcarius (Zanno, 2010) has unfused interdental plates.

91. Falcarius (Zanno, 2010) has premaxillary teeth with flat lingual surfaces.

93. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2009) has axial epipophyses which do not extend past its postzygapophyses.

95. Falcarius (Zanno, 2010) and Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2009) have cervical epipophyses placed over their postzygapophyseal facets.

96. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2009) has anterior cervical centra extending past their neural arches.

97. Falcarius (Zanno, 2010) lacks carotid processes.

99. Using my redefinition of this character, Falcarius (Zanno, 2010), Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2009) and Nothronychus (Kirkland and Wolfe, 2001) have long anterior cervical neural spines.

100. Falcarius (Zanno, 2010) is polymorphic, with only posterior cervicals having two pairs of pleurocoels.

101. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2009) lacks opisthocoelous cervicals.

102. As defined here, Nothronychus (Kirkland and Wolfe, 2001) has only a small hypapophysis.

103. Falcarius (Zanno, 2010) lacks stalked posterior dorsal parapophyses.

104. Nothronychus (Kirkland and Wolfe, 2001) has hyposphene-hypantrum articulations.

106. Beipiaosaurus (Zanno, 2010) has posterior dorsals without pleurocoels. Falcarius is said to lack middle and posterior dorsal pleurocoels (Benson et al., 2011), and a posterior dorsal is illustrated without one (Zanno, 2010), so it is coded as lacking a fully pleurocoelous dorsal series.

107. Falcarius (Zanno, 2010) has long anterior dorsal transverse processes.

108. Falcarius (Zanno, 2010) has posterior dorsal neural spine tables. Nothronychus should not be coded because the only dorsal neural spine preserved is the first (Zanno et al., 2009).

110. Beipiaosaurus had five sacrals based on its ilium length (Xu et al., 2003). Falcarius may have had more than five sacrals, as only four are preserved (Zanno, 2010).

111. Falcarius (Zanno, 2010) has a sacral neural platform of fused zygapophyses.

112. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2003) has a ventrally grooved fifth sacral centrum.

113. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2003) lacks pleurocoels in its last two sacrals at least.

114. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2003) lacks a procoelous last sacral. Falcarius (Zanno, 2010) can not be coded, as the last sacral is not preserved.

115. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2003) has a caudal transition point.

116. Though the caudals of Falcarius are disarticulated, the one in Zanno's (2010) figure 9L has a transverse process and is more elongated than the twelfth in Beipiaosaurus, indicating Falcarius probably had more than ten caudals with transverse processes.

117. Falcarius (Zanno, 2010) has round proximal caudal centra.

120. Falcarius (Zanno, 2010) and Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2003) have short distal caudal prezygapophyses.

121. Both Falcarius (Zanno, 2010) and Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2003) have over twenty-five caudals, but contra Kirkland et al. it does not seem possible to say the former definitely had less than forty.

122. While the nine known chevrons of Falcarius are disarticulated, three of them have very elongate shafts (Zanno, 2010), suggesting the first ten chevrons were not greatly shortened. The same is true of Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2003).

123. The distal chevrons of Falcarius (Zanno, 2010) are not bifurcated anteriorly or posteriorly, and Kirkland et al. may have been confusing the dorsal processes for anterior bifurcation.

124. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2009) has cervical ribs longer than its centra. The cervical ribs of Falcarius may have extended posterior to the centrum (Zanno, 2010).

125. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2009) lacks ossified uncinate processes.

132. Falcarius (Zanno, 2010) has a hypocleidium. Zanno (2010) correctly notes that a small hypocleidium would probably not show up in the depression which is all that remains of Beipiaosaurus' central furcula.

133. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2009) lacks a laterally everted acromion. Falcarius (Zanno, 2006) has a laterally everted acromion, based on the preserved distal portion.

134. Falcarius (Zanno, 2006) and Beipiaosaurus (unpublished photo of IVPP V11559) have a subglenoid fossa on the coracoid.

135. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2009) has an unfused scapulacoracoid.

136. Falcarius (Zanno, 2006) and Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2009) have a shallow coracoid.

138. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2009) has a laterally oriented glenoid.

139. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2009) and Nothronychus (Kirkland and Wolfe, 2001) have a humerus shorter than the scapula. The elements of Falcarius belong to different individuals, and as the described humerus is longer than one scapula but shorter than another (Zanno, 2006) and the skeletal reconstruction has a humerus longer than its scapula, Kirkland et al.'s coding of Falcarius as having a short humerus is rejected in favor of an uncertainty.

140. While Nothronychus' humerus has not been illustrated at an angle where the deltopectoral crest shape can be measured, it clearly does not have the greatly expanded Confuciusornis-like morphology Kirkland et al. code it for. As Kirkland and Wolfe (2001) state the crest is well developed, it is here tentatively coded as having an angle of 50-95 degrees. Similarly, Beipiaosaurus' complete humerus is only exposed in posterior view (Xu et al., 2009), but does not have a Confuciusornis-style crest, so is coded as having an angle of more than 50 degrees at least.

142. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 1999, 2009) and Nothronychus (Kirkland and Wolfe, 2001) have a short olecranon.

143. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 1999) has a transversely flat distal ulna.

145. No definite ulnare is known for Falcarius, though Zanno (2006) identified a small element as either an ulnare or intermedium (preferring the latter alternative). If it is an ulnare, comparison to Allosaurus suggests it is figured in extensor and flexor views. While Kirkland et al. code Falcarius as having a distally triangular ulnare, I prefer to leave it uncoded pending a more certain identification and orientation. Similarly, while two possible ulnares are preserved in Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 1999), their shape also best matches the extensor view of Allosaurus', and while both hands are in extensor view, the ulnares are disarticulated if correctly identified.

148. Comparing Beipiaosaurus' fully exposed unfused distal carpal (Xu et al., 1999) to the composite semilunate in Falcarius suggests the complete semilunate structure would have been about as wide as the proximal surfaces of metacarpals I and II.

149. Beipiaosaurus (unpublished photo of IVPP V11559) has a metacarpal I over half the length of metacarpal II.

153. Based on my confining this character to manual ungual I, Falcarius (Zanno, 2006) and Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 1999) lack a proximodorsal lip on that ungual.

154. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2003) has a strongly hooked preacetabular process.

156. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2003) has a slightly rounded anterior preacetabular border.

157. Falcarius (Zanno, 2010) has a weak supracetabular crest. Beipiaosaurus (coding in Xu et al., 1999) has either a weak or absent crest.

158. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 1999) has a squared postacetabular process.

160. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2003) lacks a supratrochanteric process.

161. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 1999) has a shallow brevis fossa.

162. Falcarius (Zanno, 2010) has a prominent antitrochanter.

163. Falcarius (Zanno, 2010) and Beipiaosaurus (coding in Xu et al., 1999) lack a cuppedicus fossa, so should be coded inapplicable for its extent on the pubic peduncle.

164. Falcarius (Zanno, 2010) Beipiaosaurus (coding in Xu et al., 1999) lack a cuppedicus fossa.

165. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2003) lacks a proximodorsal ischial process.

166. Due to the restriction of this character to dorsoventral curvature, Falcarius (Zanno, 2010) is recoded as having a dorsally curved ischium. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2003) also has this state.

167. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2003) and Nothronychus (Kirkland and Wolfe, 2001) have an obturator process placed near midshaft.

169. Falcarius (Zanno, 2010), Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2003) and Nothronychus (Kirkland and Wolfe, 2001) have an obturator notch.

171. Beipiaosaurus must have a high ischiopubic ratio based on the ischial length (Xu et al., 2003), despite the incomplete pubis.

172. There seems to be an unfused symphyseal surface on the left ischium of Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2003). Falcarius (Zanno, 2010) at least lacks a fused ischial symphysis.

173. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2003) and Nothronychus (Kirkland and Wolfe, 2001) have an ischial boot.

177. Falcarius (Zanno, 2010) has a pubic apron which mostly extends from the center of the shaft.

184. Nothronychus (Kirkland and Wolfe, 2001) does not preserve a femur so cannot be coded for the presence of a fourth trochanter.

186. Beipiaosaurus (Zanno, 2010) has a medial epicondyle on its femur.

189. Falcarius (Zanno, 2010) and Nothronychus (Kirkland and Wolfe, 2001) have a shallow proximomedial fibular fossa.

192. Falcarius (Zanno, 2010) lacks a medial cnemial crest.

193. Beipiaosaurus' astragalar ascending process is partially covered by the tibia (Xu et al., 1999), so it is uncertain whether it was over 75% of the astragalocalanear width.

195. Nothronychus (Kirkland and Wolfe, 2001) lacks tibiotarsal fusion.

198. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 1999) lacks a ginglymoid metatarsal II. Nothronychus (Zanno et al., 2009) does not preserve metatarsal II, so cannot be coded.

200. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 1999) is nonarctometatarsal.

201. Nothronychus lacks an enlarged pedal ungual II based on the reidentification of manual unguals as pedal unguals by Zanno et al. (2009).

203. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 1999) has a metatarsal I which does not contact its tarsus.

206. Falcarius (Zanno, 2010) has apically expanded posterior dorsal neural spines.

207. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 1999) has a manual phalanx I-1 narrower than its radius. Falcarius (Hartman, unpublished) has a wide phalanx I-1.

209. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2009) has a large surangular flange anterior to the glenoid.

210. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 1999) has a ginglymoid metacarpal I.

212. Falcarius (Zanno, 2010) lacks a kinked anterodorsal dentary margin. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2009) has one.

214. Falcarius (Zanno, 2010) has a laterally exposed brevis fossa.

215. Falcarius (Zanno, 2010) lacks a vertical ridge on its proximolateral femur, perhaps miscoded due to Hwang et al.'s choice of state numbers.

217. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2009) has a fully toothed dentary. Nothronychus (Kirkland et al., 2001) probably has some dentary teeth based on the illustrated tooth resembling Erlikosaurus' anterior dentary teeth, but whether its dentary was fully toothed is unknown.

218. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2009) lacks a deep notch below the coracoid glenoid.

220. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2009) and Nothronychus (Kirkland and Wolfe, 2001) lack a scapular supraglenoid buttress.

222. Falcarius (Smith et al., 2011) has close set basal tubera. Nothronychus lacks basal tubera (Kirkland et al., 2005), so should be coded inapplicable.

223. Ornitholestes (pers. obs.) lack subcondylar recesses. Gorgosaurus (Bakker et al., 1988), Garudimimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005), Zanabazar (Norell et al., 2009), Troodon (Currie, 1985), Velociraptor (Norell et al., 2004) and Archaeopteryx (Alonso et al., 2004) have subcondylar recesses. Dromiceiomimus (Tahara and Larsson, 2011) is polymorphic. Oviraptor (unpublished photo) does not preserve the occipital area ventrolateral to the occipital condyle.

224. Kirkland et al. code "Ventral surface of dentary straight or nearly straight (0) or descends strongly posteriorly (1)" as only present in therizinosaurs, but the feature (which is absent in Falcarius and Segnosaurus) is an illusion caused by two variables which are already coded for. First, the strongly triangular dentary causes the posteroventral margin to be highly angled to the dorsal margin. Second, the decurved ramus means the mandible is usually illustrated with the posterior dentaty facing more ventrally, since the convention is to have the glenoid and dentary tip placed at approximately the same level. The character is thus rejected.

225. Sinosauropteryx (Currie and Chen, 2001), Compsognathus (Peyer, 2006), Struthiomimus (Nicholls and Russell, 1985), Dromiceiomimus (Osborn, 1916), Caudipteryx (Zhou et al., 2000), Microraptor (Hwang et al., 2002) and Rahonavis (O'Connor and Forster, 2010) have a small entepicondyle. Ornitholestes (unpublished photos) and Patagonykus (Novas, 1997) have a large entepicondyle.

226. Gorgosaurus (Lambe, 1917), Struthiomimus (Osnorn, 1916), Dromiceiomimus (Osborn, 1916), Anserimimus (coding in Kobayashi, 2004), Caudipteryx (coding in Gishlick, 2002) and Rinchenia (coding in Maryanska et al., 2002) have distally oriented humeral condyles. Tyrannosaurus (Carpenter and Smith, 2001), Sinosauropteryx (Currie and Chen, 2001), Ornitholestes (unpublished photos), Avimimus (Kurzanov, 1987), Sinovenator (coding in Ji et al., 2005), Microraptor (Hwang et al., 2002), Velociraptor (pers. obs. of IGM 100/986), Deinonychus (Ostrom, 1969), Rahonavis (O'Connor and Forster, 2010) and Archaeopteryx (Wellnhofer, 1974) have anteriorly oriented condyles.

227. Shuvuuia (pers. obs. of IGM 100/1276), Mononykus (Perle et al., 1994), Chirostenotes (Currie and Russell, 1988), Microvenator (Makovicky and Sues, 1998), IGM 100/42 (unpublished photo), "Ingenia" (unpublished photo), Saurornitholestes (Hutchinson, 2001), Deinonychus (Ostrom, 1969), Unenlagia (Gianechini and Apesteguia, 2011) and Rahonavis (unpublished photos) lack a deeply socketed ilioischial articulation. Allosaurus (Gilmore, 1920; Madsen, 1976), Ornitholestes (unpublished photos), Gorgosaurus (Lambe, 1917), Shenzhousaurus (Ji et al., 2003) and Garudimimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005) have a deeply socketed ilioischial articulation.

228. Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 2001) and Microraptor (Xu et al., 2000) have compressed tooth roots. Harpymimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005) has circular tooth roots. Taxa without lateral teeth should be coded inapplicable- Garudimimus, Gallimimus, Struthiomimus, Dromiceiomimus, Caudipteryx, Avimimus, Chirostenotes, Oviraptor, Rinchenia, IGM 100/42, Conchoraptor, "Ingenia" and Confuciusornis.

229. Garudimimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005), Archaeornithomimus (Smith and Galton, 1990), Shuvuuia (pers. obs. of IGM 100/975), Rinchenia (unpublished photo), Sinovenator (Xu et al., 2002) and Sinornithosaurus (Xu et al., 1999) lack a flared preacetabular process. Compsognathus (Ostrom, 1978; Peyer, 2006), Mononykus (Perle et al., 1994) and Incisivosaurus (Xu et al., 2002) cannot be coded.

230. Though Kirkland et al. differentiate the states as teeth "mediolaterally flattened and recurved" versus "lanceolate and subsymmetrical", lanceolate teeth like those of therizinosaurs are mediolaterally flattened, so this character is refined to only score for recurvature. While only dentary teeth are specified, I also include lateral maxillary teeth in my coding. Pelecanimimus (coding in Kobayashi, 2004), Sinovenator (Xu et al., 2002), IGM 100/44 (Barsbold et al., 1987), Microraptor (Hwang et al., 2002) and Tsaagan (Norell et al., 2006) have recurved teeth. Shenzhousaurus (Ji et al., 2003), Shuvuuia (Dufeau, 2003) and Mononykus (Perle et al., 1993) lack recurved teeth. Falcarius (Zanno, 2010), Beipiaosaurus (Xu et al., 1999), Segnosaurus (Barsbold and Maryanska, 1990) and Archaeopteryx (Howgate, 1984) are polymorphic. Taxa without lateral teeth should be coded inapplicable- Garudimimus, Gallimimus, Struthiomimus, Dromiceiomimus, Caudipteryx, Avimimus, Chirostenotes, Oviraptor, Rinchenia, IGM 100/42, Conchoraptor, "Ingenia" and Confuciusornis.

231. This character is a composite involving both the size and labiolingual compression of anterior dentary teeth. As most theropods have less compressed anterior teeth, only size is used here. It is thus made a new state of Norell et al.'s (2001) character 90 coding for smaller anterior teeth. Harpymimus (Kobayashi and Barsbold, 2005), Incisivosaurus (Xu et al., 2002), Microraptor (Ji, 2002) and Tsaagan (Norell et al., 2006) lack enlarged anterior teeth. Pelecanimimus (Perez-Moreno et al., 1994), Shuvuuia (Dufeau, 2003) and Beipiaosaurus (coding in Xu et al., 1999) have enlarged anterior teeth. Mononykus (Perle et al., 1994) and Achillobator (Perle et al., 1999) cannot be coded. Taxa without dentary teeth should be coded inapplicable- Garudimimus, Gallimimus, Struthiomimus, Dromiceiomimus, Caudipteryx, Avimimus, Chirostenotes, Microvenator, Oviraptor, Rinchenia, IGM 100/42, Conchoraptor, "Ingenia" and Confuciusornis.
